Then remove all the cotton and treat the wound with an appropriate ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like scrofula, they should be treated as we have described for fissures of scrofula. If the wound becomes pus-filled, then apply cautery as we have described earlier.
de la routure de l’artere	of bleeding from the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is swollen and the skin on top is tight, this often causes an abscess, and likewise there is swelling and abscess in the vein; and one can recognize it when it is due to the artery, as the abscesses are long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a tugging; and when it is due to a vein, there is a hard lump beneath the skin; and it is foolishness to cover this abscess, especially when it is below the breast and under the armpit and in the neck and many other places, as it is very serious.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore one must avoid the cautery of iron, and if it is on the neck, one should also avoid cauterizing the head; and when it is swelling due to an artery under the skin, cut through the skin along the length of the artery; then open the artery from its origin, and carefully separate the artery from the surrounding tissue until it is exposed; then insert a needle underneath the skin where the artery is located, and pierce all the way through to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places according to what I taught you regarding the extraction of the two arteries in the temples; then puncture the area between the two threads with an instrument so that the blood inside flows out, and the abscess is relieved; then apply a poultice made of warm wine and oil, and treat it with bandages and ointments until it heals; and if the abscess is due to a vein, one should take some of the pus from the abscess and smear it all over the skin, then insert a needle underneath where he is holding the pus in his hand, and pierce through to the other side, and tie a double thread to the needle so that you can pull it through; then bind the abscess as I instructed, at either of the two ends of the thread; and if one doubts that the thread will hold, insert another needle at the same place through both threads underneath the entire abscess, and tie the threads in four places; then lance the abscess so that the pus flows out, then lance the skin and leave what is bound; then apply a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, and treat it with bandages and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, as abscesses come to the artery and vein, so they come to the nerves when they are injured or through excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and elbows and all over where there are joints, and it is a painful abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in various conditions without pain; and when one presses it firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but under the skin; and it is mute in all parts, and does not go forward or backward, or downward or upward, and that which is in joints should not be covered with iron: otherwise there might be contraction; and that which is on the head or forehead, treat with a plaster.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and squeeze it at its root; and if it is large, pierce it with an awl, and scrape it, then cut out the wound and sew it up, and let it heal.
des grosses boces pendans	of large bumps hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	At times they appear in the belly and nowhere else; it is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to ears, with thin roots and thick leaves. There are small ones and very large ones; I saw a man who had two on his belly that looked more like fungi than anything else, without any difference, white in color, with fine roots, and split open, from which moisture flowed.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found one weighing 18 ounces and the other 6, and the treatment for the incision is such that you examine whether the disease is moist, and the color of the arthrous is white and moist with fine roots; then cut with a spatulum widely, and have at hand the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For often there is excessive bleeding when cutting, and if the blood flows, then hurry to cauterize it; and if you see that the disease is terrified and fearful of the iron incision, take a well-prepared piece of plaster, and cover the arthrous as we have said, and leave it for two days; then restrain it, and do not stop squeezing the plaster until he cuts the arthrous, and pieces come out through it without effort; and if the roots are thick, then be careful about cutting them directly on the belly, but you can certainly cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and beware of covering the belly which is of a pale color and of poor sense and of milky aspect.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the ulcer next.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil bursts
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from a cautery on a wound or from a fissure in the syphilis, and it is on the belly and some of the bowels, as happens with other sores, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is mentioned earlier, or from flatulence; and if it is from the fissure of the syphilis and from the discharge of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens with varied discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is through the intestinal opening, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with their fingers, it pops back out, and then it comes back in, and sometimes it is serrated, and grows larger at the entrance of the anus due to strong effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a minor issue and opens easily when you press it with your hand, and does not constrict; and if it is due to blood, then the abscesses are large and firm, and are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to flatulence, then there is swelling on touching, and the work involves checking whether the appearance is due to arterial or venous blood, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you need to let the wound heal.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is in the intestine or the bladder, then you should tell the patient to tighten his belt and stretch out straight, then sign all around the stomach; then command him to lie still between your hands, then go around the area that you have marked on the scrotum, then open up half of the abscess at the top by the large nail; then tie it tightly all around with a strong thread or strong silk string, and let the patient's testicles hang free; then open up half of the abscess stretched out over the string, and insert your finger, and feel for the intestine; if you find it caught in the string, loosen it and pull the intestine out from inside the body; and if you find the bladder, catch it at the nail and cut away the excess; and if the artery or vein acts contrary, go about your business and take two needles, and thread two strong pieces of thread through them, and pierce what you have made in a cross so that you can create an opening; then pull out the abscess in four places using the needles, and if you see anything, remove the needles and leave the area alone so that it may drain, and cut away the dead flesh when it becomes soft and drained, then treat the wound as we have said; and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the area as needed, and sew it up.
dou chancre	of sores
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have already discussed the types of sores, how to treat them with medicine, and how to avoid using iron in the treatment. Now let us speak of sores that occur in the mouth, and great care must be taken in treating them. The ancients say that when a sore is in a place where it can be easily reached, as in the breast, armpit, or similar areas, it should be completely removed at the beginning. However, if the sore is large and old, you should not touch it, for I have never seen one healed, nor has anyone else before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the sore is in a place that can be easily reached, as we have said, the treatment is to first purging the patient of black bile; then let the wound bleed if it shows signs of repletion; then clean the wound and cut away the dead tissue from around the sore; then stop any bleeding with cauterization; finally, treat the wound further until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed in the division the appearances of dropsy, and how the gathering of water occurs, and the signs of each appearance, and the treatment that is carried out by medicine, and that which is cured by iron; only this is clarified: one should not use iron for these two appearances: namely, tympanites and yposarche, as it is a deadly matter. Therefore, when you treat this appearance of dropsy called 'eclites' with medicine, and the cure does not help, then consider if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as stomach problems and similar conditions; in this case, do not use iron, as there is a risk involved. But if you see that the patient is of strong constitution, and they only have dropsy without any other illness, and they are not too young or too old, then you should proceed as follows: raise the patient upright on your hands, and press their belly to force the water to the lowest part of the feet, then take the spiny spathumile according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And take two parts of the powder.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Take a pointed instrument, and make sure it is not so sharp that it pierces all the way through to the intestines when inserted, nor so blunt that it does not penetrate; then examine if the hydrops is located near the intestines. If it is due to a liver ailment, make your incision on the left side of the belly three fingers below the nipple; and if it is due to a lung issue, make the incision on the right side. It is important that the patient does not lie on the incision so that the fluids do not flow towards the affected area. Then, pierce through the skin with your instrument, insert the tube, and lift your hand as you would when skinning an animal to the thickness of a fingernail or an inch all around; then pierce the chest wall until the fluid comes out at the desired location, which is where the water is located. Then, pull out the tube and insert your instrument again to remove any excess fluid.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	It resembles a silver-tipped cane, made of lightweight bronze or brass, with a small hole in the lower part. On one side there are three holes, on another two, on another one, and on the last side, one; the head is shaped like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes make when cutting a quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	at the top is the outlet, so that when the instrument comes to a boil, it releases immediately onto the instrument; empty half or a third of it, because if you empty more than it needs in that hour, the patient may die from the shock of the liquid, or he may faint or approach death; but empty according to the quantity of its strength, and according to what the dispositions of the illness indicate, and his pulses; then withdraw the instrument and hold back the liquid, which is now retained by the membrane that blocks the hole above the syphon, about which I have spoken, and pierce it according to this method; then reintroduce the instrument the next day if you see the patient can bear it, and withdraw a little liquid; do this every day, and be careful not to overdo it as long as there is even a little liquid left.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the disease, and leave it for a long time with much water, and treat it with hot sand or ash, and with sweat or bath, and in the sun, and if he becomes thirsty; and treat it with desiccation medicines until he is healed, and cauterize the stomach and liver and spleen after extracting the fluid, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	from the congestion of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without a foreskin, or with a small one, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If necessary, cut it open immediately with a very sharp spatula according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put a thin plug of wax in the foreskin and hold it there for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug, and he will urinate, and then replace it; and sometimes it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out pushes the foreskin open.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose orifices are small, if they are medicated with lead plaster as we have said, will be enlarged.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have an orifice in their place are blocked. Some are born with an orifice at the head of the penis, which prevents them from urinating unless they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the urethra, and this is a serious condition.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies on his back, then the head of the penis and foreskin are cut to the size of a feather, so that the incision falls in the middle, as it should be; and take care to prevent bleeding which often occurs, and if it does happen, then stop the flow of blood with a cautery, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blisters come on the penis, and it is an unsightly appearance of pus; and there are harmful and harmless ones; therefore you should lance them with a very sharp knife, and clean and dry them thoroughly, then apply cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then treat it with fine ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, discolored and foul-smelling, then you should apply a cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the ulcer is on the shaft of the penis, and part of it is inside and part outside, then you must first remove the ulcer that is inside; and when it is healed, treat the external portion.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, if the foreskin is not assured so that it is not pierced, and blackness and corruption come in his penis and scrotum; then everything that is black and corrupt should be cut away, then bind on the ointment of honey and flour made from pomegranate peel and walnuts, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if there is bleeding, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauteries have two uses together: that is, for bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must tie a string around the penis and let the patient urinate through it; and when the skin becomes sore at the tip of the penis due to an injury or an abscess, you should then cut it with an instrument, as long as the foreskin is loose and released from all sides, and if it is painful to discuss this, you should cut it with a spatulum at some point on the head of the penis and the glans; then separate them gently, and place a thin linen cloth moistened in cold water between them so that they do not adhere again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a natural process like other wounds; however, when we perform this act intentionally, especially on infants, it is necessary for us to do our best and with the least harm possible.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention the circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen the majority of masters and surgeons who made circumcision around the glans, and on many, and on all a new foreskin; then the skin would heal because there are two membranes, and sometimes one above and one below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now they cover it again, and the pain is doubled, and in the cleansing of the glans there is no assurance that the tip of the member is cleansed; and in the cleansing of the nail sometimes the iron slips and ruins the work, and many times they grow without needing to be cleansed, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the cleansing that is done around the glans, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut justly both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, you cut evenly in I all the way; but let the thread be well wrapped around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the pole, and then let him pull it in every way he can; then let him stand between your hands straight up, and support his weight between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the pole and breathe on the heart, and draw it up as far as the heart is in; then cleanse it well from the dirt that has gathered there, then tie the place marked with a double thread, then tie it under I to the other string; and hold it by both hands by the second binding to the pouch and to the index finger, and pull between the two strings, then lift the heart gently and draw the head of the pole; then let the blood run little by little, for that is the wound; and put powder on top of the powder, a cloth glued with an egg cooked in rose water, confited with good fresh rosemary oil, and leave it until the next day, and heal it with another healing until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces for cleansing is such that the two heads are tense and sharp, and the heads are as large as the palm evenly:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	the error of the purification is when the vein within bleeds upon incision; therefore you should stretch it with your thumbnail so that the vein becomes an abscess; and then cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your thumbnail, hold it with tweezers and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it bleeds for three days and what is under the foreskin is swollen, then leave it until the abscesses are soothed and the skin is lightly scabs over; then cut it as much as you can move it, and be careful of the part of the foreskin, it will not harm it in any way.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Heal therefore the site of such a wound with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if it cuts too deeply into the foreskin and goes above it, it will not harm; then heal it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	from retention of urine:
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to a stone, or frozen blood, or a tumor, or similar conditions which we have mentioned in the previous sections. If the urine is not released and you see that the obstruction is caused by a stone lodged in the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be made to bend forward and rest his knees; his feet should be placed on his back, and he should press his abdomen from above the back, and strain as hard as he can. This will force the neck of the bladder upward and facilitate the passage of the stone, releasing the urine. If this does not work as described, and the patient feels great pain, then you must use an instrument called a "syringe", which is crafted as follows: it should be made of thin silver, as light as a bird's feather; the tube should be about a palm and a half in length, with a fine point.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the emission of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie to the end a little wool or cotton, and insert the end of the thread into the syringe; and squeeze out the excess wool and insert it into the syringe up to the top, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a chair, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the scrotum; then fill the syringe up to the bladder, and feel the patient urinate into the void, and if this is not done according to this order, it is because the person guiding where it goes is doing it wrong; then pull out the thread through all the wool, and the urine follows the wool, then withdraw it, and let the urine flow; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or blood comes in the bladder, or pus is gathered there, and you see it distilling with water and medicine, then do this to all the instrument which is called "clepsydra", and it is formed:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you can see; the hair-like channels through which the medicine works are such that it blocks the penis without addition, so that one can draw out moisture and insert it when necessary; and when you see your medicines moving in the bladder, place the tip of the catheter in the moisture and draw it up using the string attached to it; then the moisture will be drawn into the catheter, and the patient will feel it; this is the form of the subtle catheter used to catheterize the bladder: thus it is made:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is made of silver or brass, and the tip is higher up; and under it there is a testicle or an egg-sized lump; then take a lamb's bladder and put the medicine you want to use to catheterize the bladder in it, then tie it between the two testicles with a strong double thread, and heat this medicine over a fire; then insert the tip of the catheter into the penis, then press your hand on the bladder to draw the medicine up gently, until the patient feels that the medicine has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make it into a circle, and pierce a hole in it all around; then thread a strong string through these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a ball, and put in it what you want of oil and medicine and water, and attach it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the medicine reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division of stones, and their extraction together with medicines; and I have told the difference between a stone lodged in the ureter, and all the signs, and in which kind of stone one should operate with cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder happens most often to children, and it is a sign that the water goes out of the bladder resembling water in its subtlety; and they open their eyes widely, and feel pain in their penis, and can urinate many times, and then become constipated; and many of these have hernia; and healing is easier for children until they are four years old, and it is much more painful in the elderly, and is middle-aged in those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the feces which are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes clogs up when seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and lift him up and move him around so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes it comes out from the top; then let him sit between your hands, which are prepared, and his hands should be under his thighs so that the bladder is completely tilted downward; then probe and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the urethra, then hasten now to cut upon the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out with the touch, then moisten your left index finger with oil, if the patient is fat, or your middle finger if the patient is slender and young; then insert it into his anus, and probe for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, draw it up to the neck of the bladder; then press on your finger and draw it out where you intend to cut.Et s’il chiet au touchier dou tout, si le fai seoir droit et la quier a son fondement, et li quier li col de la vessie, et le bouton sus a sa main dreite, si que la vessie soit inclinans aval; puis tu l’esprouves s’il ne chiet au touc.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press upon the bladder with his hand, and tell the patient to extend his testicles upward with his right hand, and with his left hand pull back the skin underneath the testicles in the area where the incision will be made; then insert the spatulum tightly, for this is its purpose:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And they do it between what is between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side of the navel; and it should be straight on the stone, and your fingers should be at the anus, and the incision should be across the navel so that it is wide at the top and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; by chance, the press on the finger which is in the anus may cause it to pop out without effort; and know that there is some stone which has angles and edges: then it is easy to remove; and there is some which is below, like a grape, and round, whose removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And so with the one which has angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not pop out, then you must grip it with pincers which are as sharp as a file at the tip, to pull out the stone so that it does not escape; or you push underneath it a thin instrument curved at the end; and if you cannot grab it thus, then enlarge the opening, and if the blood bursts, then constrict it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, then insert the largest one first into the neck of the bladder, then pull it out, then the next largest, and so on if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then one must shave it, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things can happen to the patient: either they die or the urine comes out through the wound that the urethra cannot heal; but nevertheless, try to pull it out with tweezers, as much as you can pull it out in pieces; and when you have finished your work, anoint the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and constrict it, and put a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water on top to soothe the hot abscess; then resow the wound on his thigh, and do not remove the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, wash the area well with oil and water, then treat the wound with thin ointment and thick ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses and corrosion of blood in the bladder occur, and it is retained by this means: push your finger into the wound, and draw out that blood, for if any remains, the bladder will be corroded and burst; then raise the wound with water and garlic and salt, and aid him in every way you know until he is healed; and it is necessary to tie his two thighs together with cords, assembling the remedies on the wound, every day you treat it.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small and it is in the urethra, and fixed there, and the urine cannot pass; then the treatment of what I have said before, that you should cut it many times, is sufficient for the cutting by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take an iron needle according to this shape and let it have three angles bent into a tinder:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis under the stone, so that it cannot return to the bladder; then push the probe into the penis gently, until it reaches the stone; then turn the probe in your hand within the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side; then urine will come at once, then press your hand on what is left of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken at once and comes out with the urine, then the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this by any means that push against the stone, then tie a thread under the stone and another above it, then make an incision in the penis where the stone is between the two threads, then pull the stone out, and untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it heals.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Sometimes stones become lodged in women's bodies, and if this happens, the treatment is difficult due to three reasons: first, the woman might be a virgin; second, one cannot find an experienced woman who will examine her, especially if she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well skilled in this art of midwifery; and the fourth way is that the woman's stone is more deeply embedded than a man's, so it needs to be cut more deeply, and there is great fear involved. And if necessity arises, one should take a midwife who is very experienced, and with difficulty persuade her, and if you cannot persuade her, then take a subtle mirror; and show her a wise woman experienced in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command in the examination of the stone; and be sure to look carefully to see if the woman is a virgin. Then she should push her finger into the vagina and feel for the stone; and if she finds it, she should press it beneath her finger, and recommend that she push her finger or the tip of her finger into the wound, and hold and press her left hand firmly over the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she is constipated, she should move her bowels little by little from the bladder to below, until she reaches the root of the thigh; then press on the stone at the root of the thigh towards the middle, where the ureter is located and feels the stone in that area; and do not move your finger above or below the stone, and start with a small incision; then insert the probe into the incision, feeling for the stone until it can be pushed out, and know that there are many types of stones: small and large, smooth and sharp, long and round, and those with bumps.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	then you will know their similarities to identify the problem.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood vessels bleed, put ground vitriol on the spot and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your task until the stone is out, and have the tools I told you about in the extraction of stones for men to help you with your work; and if the bleeding vessel is cut, put the powder on the site and apply pressure with bandages and bands, and do not re-open it, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, or the patient might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the place healed, return to your work until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	of carnous hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquous effusion is nothing else but the collection of moisture or white pus, which is under the heart of the testicles, and contains the egg; and is called "pus", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one believes that it is another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white pus that we have mentioned; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the cause of this disease is due to weakness that comes from the testicles, and this matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors; it is either jaundice-like, or red, black, watery white, and so on; these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is in the white syphilis that we have said, then the abscesses are reason, small as long as the figure of an egg, and does not open the testicles, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the fabric itself, then the abscesses are reason with part of an egg, and because of this they think it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white syphilis, then one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, test all the ways in which the shape comes before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, then, what comes after the entrance, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient should be bled according to their strength and the fullness of their body; then he lies on his back on something slightly raised, and many layers of cloth are placed underneath him; then he sits up on his left side, and the assistant sits on his right, and extends the arm to one of the two ribs of the heart; then take the spatulum and cut the skin of the ribs in between them from the top all the way down to the nipple, and the incision should be straight while cutting the skin of the ribs up to the white fat, and it is carefully peeled according to its strength; then pierce the fat with a large hole and draw out all the water, and then place your fingers on it, and hold the fat in place; and do not touch the heart, only the fat; cut it all the way around in sections, being careful to bleed profusely, or the water will return; and if the egg pops out during your work, put it back in its place when you have finished working on the fat; then bring the two edges of the skin of the ribs together with a single stitch, and then treat it like any other wound until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then you should ligate the vessels that are suspended, fearing the flow of blood; then cut the testicle all the way around at the suspension, and draw out the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if pus is gathered in two parts together, know that they are two blisters; then press the other part as you did the first equally, then wash out the blood, and put into the wound soft lamb's wool soaked in rose oil; and put on another piece of soft lamb's wool soaked in wine and oil, and place it over the two blisters, and put over that doubled linen, and tie it around to everything according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two pieces of linen and stuff them with lamb's wool according to this form and let them be sewn together at the crotch of the breeches, and let one of the heads press upon the bottom up to the back, and the other at the part of the buttock; and let the other two heads be over the two angles, and let all be tied together by the buckle of the breeches; and sometimes this blister is treated with cautery instead of iron. And it is that you press the chisel-like cautery gently upon the skin of the blisters, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white pus containing the water is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce the pus sacs at the edges, and scorch them with this fine hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cup in every way that you can, as long as you stretch everything out; and be careful not to let the fire touch the egg; and know that this work is the safest; and move while watching for blood loss, and changes in the wound; and if nothing makes you contrary, or abscesses or blood loss or anything else, then heal what makes you contrary, according to what has already been said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this treatment due to its horror, then use perforation as I have told you, and it is that when you are certain by the signs we have mentioned that the pus-filled sac is drained, then have the patient sit on a high seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below throughout the entire spatumile, and place the perforation near the center of the body; make the holes large so all the fluid can flow out; then put cotton over the wound and bandage it, and let the remaining fluid drain, then heal the wound until it is clean; and if the white membrane does not allow the fluid to come out through the mouth of the wound, you should insert a feather or the instrument used to treat dropsy patients, whose shape is described earlier; widen the wound and know that the fluid will return, and will form again around six months later, and when it has formed as before, the patient will recover.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the apoplexy of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	You should know that in the treatment of this disease, fear leads to many complications, and that is why I think it is better to leave it untreated. But I will tell you about its treatment and the appearance of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, I say that many abscesses come from the body, especially from the groin; and there are many types of cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is what you should know: the cause can be an acute fever or a blow, and the color of the abscess depends on the color of the body; it does not hurt, and it is a serious abscess. Sometimes there are light-colored, fearful, and bloody abscesses, and sometimes they come from a ruptured artery or a swollen vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from a ruptured artery, it is recognized by the hot feeling of the abscess when you press it with your fingers; and you should not touch it.Quant il vient par enfleure de voine, si est conus, s’il est d’un color que li cors soit, ou plus clers ou plus sombres; et si tu le demures, si viendra a teins, et ne sera pas grief; et s’il viengne de voine, il sera en la place de voine.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Those who have swelling in the vein are known by their appearance and the feeling of the fingers, and anyone can do well to shape it according to this appearance and others; you should press on the top of the testicles, then they will be raised up, and the white stringy part will be drawn out, and the suspensory ligament will be released from all parts of the testicle.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the testicle is already damaged by these diseases, then you should draw out and press on it; and if there is a hernia in the scrotum or in what is inside the vessels, then you should release all that membrane and press on it roundedly.Si li syfac et le trais sodez a la tenve, si covient que tu esprimes l’uef, et li trays en bas; et s’il est sodez a li corps, si covient que tu copes l’uef, et li trays en bas.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the egg is in a rear position, you must cup it all and extract the yolk, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is finished, apply the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the apoplexy of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a hernia wrapped in a covering similar to a bulge, with the softening of the testicles, and the sick person moves painfully when he walks; and the cure of this disease is also just as fearful as the one above, and yet we will still tell you its treatment according to what the ancients did.Li ancien disent que tu covient faire l’incision de la tenve sus l’uef en bas, et delivre li syfac, et li coions en haut, et li trais, et li suspensoire; et si tu troves l’uef sodez a li corps, si covient que tu le copes et li trays en bas; et s’il est sodez a la tenve, si covient que tu le delivres de la tenve, et li trays en bas; et si tu troves li syfac dedens les coions, si covient que tu le delivre et li copes, et li trays en bas.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	Let the patient sit on an elevated seat, then tie the suspension band of the scrotum tightly with your fingers, around all the vessels near the penis, and constrict them firmly; then cut through the vessels with a sharp spatulum, widely and directly, so that they are exposed, and then scrape each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries in the temples; then insert a needle with a double thread where the vein first appeared, and tie it directly to the other end; then pull them gently according to the length of the body, following the corrupted moisture; then treat the wound as with the others, or with a bowstring, so that any vessel that is torn does not nourish one of the testicles; for this does no harm, and if the vein reaches all the vessels, then pull on the testicles at all the vessels, so that the urethra loses its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dries up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	from the rot of the sinus
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The causes of this hernia are from the incision that comes from the scrotum, or the extension on the abdomen in the region of the inguinal canal, causing the intestines to descend from this opening to one of the testicles; and this opening is in the scrotum, or from its extension, and these two types of hernias come from many causes: from percussion, or jumping, or straining, or lifting a heavy load, and similar activities; and the signs when it is from the extension of the scrotum are that it occurs little by little over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are even all the way to the bottom, because the scrotum presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are that when it is from a section of syphilis, it brings on sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear in various places under the skin, and this is due to the output of the intestines and the body's defense against syphilis.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with it, and is retained inside, causing great pain to the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, from which one should flee.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;
