et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of treatment is that you instruct the patient to draw the intestine with his hand into the wound if he can; then place your hands on his neck between your hands and lift his buttocks; then bend down the scrotum towards the navel, and grasp all the skin of the testicles from above; then insert hooks into the incision according to what you need in order to open the wound, and make it so that the ureter can come out; then scrape off the scrotum which is under the skin of the testicles, until the hard white scrotum is exposed everywhere; then put your index finger into the opening behind the testicle, between the white scrotum which is under the skin of the egg, and between the second scrotum, and separate what is behind the egg, and between the second scrotum; then move your right hand inside the scrotum, and lift up the white scrotum towards your left hand, and lift up the egg with all the scrotum towards the navel; then instruct an assistant to lift up the egg from above, and untie what is behind the bandage; then feel with your fingers if there is any intestine wrapped around the hard white scrotum, and if you find anything, put it back into the abdomen; then take a needle with a thick thread made of 10 threads, and insert it into the back part of the scrotum, which is after the skin of the testicles; then grasp the ends of the threads, so that there are 4 threads; then tie them together in the shape of a cross, and tie the scrotum with a strong band in two places; then wrap up the ends of the threads, and tie them firmly in two places, so that none of the vessels that nourish it can enter, causing an abscess to form there; then place the thread according to the first long one 2 fingers from that one, and after those two leave a space the size of a finger from the scrotum which is under the skin of the testicles; then grasp in the part which is under the skin of the testicles, so that the blood flows, as we have said before; then administer soft wool soaked in oil, and put it into the wounds, and apply the bandage which we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white syphilis that we have mentioned is cauterized after an incision, out of fear of a blood flow.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and leave the ligature in place until it cuts through; and if it takes time to fall out, use a hot water bath, and apply what we have said, until it cuts through; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of carnous hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients say that it is made like the thread that is joined to the vis, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after the incision above lightly from below; then cut them halfway through, and treat the abscess with what we have said, until the vessels fall out; then treat it as we have said, until it is completely healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes hernia occurs within the intestines, as we have said, and opens up the passageway; and no intestines fall out into the rectum, and if any do fall out it is a small amount, and they repair themselves every hour; and even if he remains in this condition for too long, he may develop an abscess in the intestines, as we have said, because the hernia is stretched and then becomes soft and swollen and opens up; and it is treated with cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is treated by iron in this way: and the patient lies on his back between your hands, then you cut the hernia open with a broad blade according to the amount of three fingers; and then extract the hernia sac which is under the skin, then take the intestinal thread and place it over the visible part of the hernia; and press it down firmly into the abdomen, then stitch up the two visible ends of the hernia sac using the intestinal thread, and stitch one side and then the other; then extract the intestinal thread, and do not cover or stretch the hernia sac or anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of intestinal hernias; then treat it with wound treatment.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, clean and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syphilitic is constrained, and has no appearance in the rut; and the cautery is better in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles becomes soft in some men because the contents within are softened, and it is milky in appearance. When one wishes to treat this, one must make the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened skin on top of the natural skin; then unite the two edges of the wound with a single stitch, or up to four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and treat it as you would any other wound until it is healed, removing the stitches.
dou chastrement	of chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You should know that castration is considered taboo in our law, and for this reason, I would prefer not to discuss it in this book. However, knowledge of castration is necessary for two reasons: first, so that the physician can answer questions about it and know how to perform the procedure; and second, because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as bulls, rams, and horses.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say, therefore, that castration is done in two ways: either by pulling or by cutting.Car il y a deux manieres de castrer; l'une par atraction, et l'autre par fendure.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method of castration by pulling, we make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles become soft and loose, then you grip them with your hand and pull until they come off.Et quant tu le veis faire, quere la beste tant qu’il soit remais; puis s’il est mort, quere li la teste et les piez, et mets la carne a cuire.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the castration of the groin: you should hold the beast, and squeeze the skin of the testicles in your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and hit each testicle once, when you have well scrotched them; and I leave some poc of the syrup and the subtle syrup which is over the vessels; and this manner of castration is worse than that which is done by attraction, because in attraction something of the testicles may remain by chance, by which the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is of two types in men: one is that between the two testicles appears as the form of nature of a woman, where there is hair, and sometimes the urine flows out.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other type is in women, and has on the groin as a penis and testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of men and women is that you dress the genitals adjusted all, and treat them as other wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the testicles
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A tent is an adjusted wound on the natural part, so that it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should dye the excess of the tentigen with your hand or fingernails, and cover it lightly; and do not go too deep, so that bleeding does not occur, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed; and for another wound that occurs at the mouth of the marris, use it, and perhaps it will jump out, and it is according to the appearance of a cow, and for this reason the ancients called it the "cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you need to treat it, as we have said before, treat it with a poultice, and heal it until it is cured.
de erratique	of Erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is errant if the nature of the woman is not understood, or the passage is small; and it is natural at birth, or accidental due to illness that comes to it; or it is caused by a foreign object, or a sore subtle or thick, and it is formed deep in the womb, or on the sides, or underneath, or wherever it may be; and they should understand conception and childbirth, and sometimes flowers as well; and knowledge of this comes from observing the dance.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is visibly close by, then use your fingers or a stick.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a sore subtle and it is close to the lips, then do this: place your two index fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then form the lips, so that the subtle sore is rolled, and cover the swelling; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it over the area; and let the woman lie at home every day, so that it may not stick.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	If the ulcer is hard and dense, then you must cut it with a spatulum similar to a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is from a recent blow, then it should be washed and cut; and have blood-stopping medicines such as aconite, dragon's blood, incense, and egg white; then apply a broad piece of wool so that the wound does not close up; and so for a long time, and then a linen bandage; then other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when there is bruising, it should be cut in this way, if it is not an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For with an abscess in the shoulder, one must not cut.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which bleed without custom, and when hemorrhoids are old they become ठठउला; and we have already said in the division their similarities to תालुल, and the signs, and I will say here those which receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thrush, when they are fully developed in the anus, and do not respond to feeling, are not healed by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the anus, which one can feel, are those that one can heal.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold room, then pull out the hemorrhoids with tweezers and cut off their roots, then powder them with medicines that constrict blood vessels, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then tie her feet to the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, have her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and gales and similar things, then take barley flour and mix it with honey and garlic, and make a poultice out of it to apply to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it is stopped, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, then make him breathe with cupping glasses on his back and breasts without bleeding them; then take wool, wet it in juice of plantain or of dogwood mixed with old wine, and apply it to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has drained, then treat the wound with ointment until it heals; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles rough ash, so cover it as I have said before; and then treat it until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses in the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscess come from the bowels, such as sores and suppurating abscesses, herpes, boils, and hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, and several other diseases that I have mentioned in the introduction.Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I describe in this treatise the hot abscess that occurs in the buttocks, which is not one of the abscesses that collect in the bowel; and if you want to know how it is treated with iron, then observe whether the abscess is soft at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and whether it turns red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not hurry to pierce it, but let the pain subside; and then let the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats on which he can lean, and support his back and press his feet against the sides of his legs; and let his buttocks be spread apart, and let him place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a cord; then suck the orifice towards the right side, and administer the instrument used to open the abscess, from which the pus will flow out afterward; and it is necessary that when you see the instrument being administered, you insert the probe first to find out the depth of the abscess so that what goes into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and so that it does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the abscess with cloth so that the instrument does not cause him distress; and let him hold the cone of the instrument up, and let him apply the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscesses are opened and they are made to the soft hand, then they should be covered with the head, or the spathomile lead; and when the bowels are emptied, then you should put in the wound moist tents in rose oil, or in dry green oil; and put the tent out of the wound at the bottom of the injury, and put over the injury and over the clean linen pad moistened with water or malves are cooked; then cure after two days of ointment coming to this, until it is healed; and sometimes lift up the injury and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and aristolochia are cooked for a long time; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed in the injury, then you should guard against cooking with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary for the midwife to first know the natural form of childbirth, and the signs indicate when you see the woman pushing downward, and wanting to smell the aroma: then the child hurries to exit; thus you know that this childbirth is according to nature, and the placenta follows the baby, and the membranes come with it; and when you see these signs, one should gently press her belly so that the child emerges quickly; for when he exits from her womb, the placenta follows him, and the mother's superfluities are cleansed by good purification; and this one who comes out in a different way does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes the baby emerges feet first, or from the chest, hands, or stomach; it may emerge from the side, or in other bad positions; thus the midwife must be wise and cunning in these matters, and beware of errors and deception, and I will show you all the forms and how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out through the head in a natural way, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her strength is weak, then let her sit on a low stool or have women hold her up; and let her drink a cup of rose water in which has been cooked oil or fenugreek, and then let the midwife put between her lips the small spatula of which I will now give the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the membrane, and press against its nail until the moisture that is within flows out; and squeeze the belly of the woman so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, one should give the woman an enema with a poultice of fenugreek with castor oil; then make her sniff and sneeze with incense, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: then the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the hands come out, you should gently pull them back in a little bit at a time; and if they cannot go in, put the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up; then tilt the stool so that she does not urinate while standing; and if the hands still cannot go in, and the child is dead, grab their hands with the knife placed as described earlier, and pull out the child, and reset everything as before.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the delivery of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out on its feet, it should be pushed up; and then rock it gently back and forth until it is straightened out; then grab one of its feet and stretch it gently back and forth.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up to the crotch, instruct it to grab hold, and make it sneeze from the neck; if it jumps out, so be it, if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump out as we have said, then draw it back little by little, until it is according to its natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easy.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have described, take some mastic, and oil of six months old, and melted gum, and grind them all in a mortar; and spread this ointment on the woman's privates, then let her sit in warm water up to her ribcage; and when she is soft down there, put a collar of myrrh around her waist and tie it on tightly, and leave it for an hour; then have her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and squeeze her mouth and nose gently, and lightly press her belly, for the child will come out now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's birth onto his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this way, put your hands on its bottom gently; then lie it on its side, with its feet hanging down, and let it lie on its bed; and fold its hands gently, and then press its hands on its belly, and take away the cushions underneath, until it is laid flat; and if the child does not cry out, then take its feet and move them about, and then move its belly upwards, and then put your hands in; and rock the child gently; and command the woman to hold on until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the birth of the child, which comes out, wide, one hand at a time
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I will tell you how to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her sit on the bed, and raise her legs straight; then bring the mustard plaster that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a chair, and then try to bring back the hand; and rock the child according to its natural shape, and make her sneeze, and command her to hold on until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child's emergence onto his neck, and have spread his hands, and turned his face towards his mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I want the patient to hold their hand out, then slowly turn it, and flex it gently; and when it is even, put on a poultice of mustard and oil, as we have said, then instruct them to move it slowly; and when you have done this, have them sit on a chair, and instruct them to grab something; and make them sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way with all the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it has come out in this way completely, then press on the afterbirth with your fingernail, until the moisture is expelled; and if the child can lean its face and neck forward, press on its chest so that it is not retained and the child dies; then put the child back inside, as you have placed it correctly, and instruct the woman to grab something a few times; then release her gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the twin's birth
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You should know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	These are strange creatures, and they do not live long if not named; I know that they multiply and are separated by the syrup that divides them, which is tied to the womb; and sometimes they emerge as naturally as a tadpole, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge quickly, the midwife should act as we have said, and be skilful, and do quickly and lightly what she does; and she should act thus as it benefits their health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the sea: one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and they are all shaped like children according to the measure of the glorious sage, and it is necessary for the midwife to know all this because by chance something similar might happen; so act according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you cure a woman of a dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and no force comes out, and you are compelled to work with your hands; then it is necessary that you know whether the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident where she fears death; then the woman must be supported on her back, and her shoulders inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the midwife applies the unguent to both parts, or lies her in bed so that she is not exposed to falling of the child; then rub the mouth of the mother with moist oils mixed with myrrh and fenugreek and linseed, then anoint the midwife's hands with these oils and unguents; then insert them gently into the mother, then press the place where she inserts the fingers so that they may be suitable for this, and take care lest the child comes out onto its head; then insert the fingers into her mouth or throat or palace or under the beard or in the armpit or near the sides, and if the delivery is at the feet, insert them into the heel and the shins; and it is necessary that she holds the unguent in her right hand, and places the cloth between her fingers of the left hand, and inserts it gently all over her hand, and inserts the finger into one of these places that we have mentioned, until she reaches the empty space; and this is the form of the unguent:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then insert it into the other hip, or in the third if you need to, so that the extractions are even; and then they should be even as they move from side to side to exit, and the hips should bite to hold them in place, just like this is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, then anoint the bottom of one of his fingers with oil and insert it into that part, and pull out the other part; and if nothing remains, then put this hip or a higher one, and do this until he excretes everything forcefully.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot return due to the constriction, then you must wrap it with a cloth until it comes out completely; then pull on the joint of the wrist or the elbow, and you should do this for the other hand and feet as well.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is tight in the passage, or if there is great pain gathered at the head, then you must push the spathula between your fingers, open up the head, and draw out the fluid; or pierce it with the instrument called "almidach", through which the shape comes with instruments or the chapter that follows this one; and in the same way proceed if the child has a naturally large head; then pull out the bones with tongs, and if the head pops out and is forced out of joint, split it so that the moisture that is in the lower passage flows out; and if it cannot emerge, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it so that the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on his feet, then the pulse is weak and the breath comes easily.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is stuck in the belly or the foot, then you should pull it out by the cloth wrapped around his hand; and make an incision in the belly or the foot, so that the moisture inside flows out; and if other members are stuck and the excrement remains, he should insert his hand into the depth of the wound and pull it out to the mouth of the wound; then he inserts a claw or two and pulls it out; and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has formed there, one should not work on it, but rather apply moist and fatty things; and the provider should apply poultices, and soak them in warm and softening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the fetus is on his side, and you can bring it to a normal position, then administer what we have said for a living child; but if one cannot, then pull it out in pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the patient is affected by those abscesses that come in the sea, and blood oozing occurs, let it be immersed in water restricting movement, and give him other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose child had been dead in her womb; then another was sewn upon it and the other died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time she got an abscess on her breast, which swelled up so much that it broke open and began to discharge.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the priest, and I thought long, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong吸引plaster, and out came a bone, and then after a few days some more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very merveilled, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I treated the wound and put my hand in so that the woman was in a better state; and she walked around for a long time like this, and sometimes she would slightly bend forward from the waist; and I have only mentioned this chapter because when the master encounters a strange condition, he should know how to provide a remedy.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the dislocation back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the press, with which one is bound in books; and at two turns around two shoulders of the two lines.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horn should be more subtle than the constrictor, and it should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the instrument should be two fingers wide, and the edges of the wood should be half a palm long or a little more; and between the two pieces there should be two adjustments of this same wood, which are firmly attached at both ends, half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the sea to open it when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, with its appearance more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony wood or boxwood, according to the appearance of tongs; and has at its two ends two adjustments, as you see, a palm-width long, and two fingers wide; and when you see open the wound to all the instrument, then let the woman lie on the bed, her feet hanging and her legs open, then insert the two adjustments adjusted together into the wound, and hold the head of the instrument between her thighs; then work your hand through the entire instrument, as you did with the tongs equally, according to the quantity that you see open the mouth of the wound, until the midwife does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all decorated and have many variations in appearance; and when the surgeon has prepared them, his work is all the faster and more efficient for it, and it is also more impressive to his patients because of their variety.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair about the instrument that you have not yet prepared, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold in her breath, and then make her sneeze with a scent, and hold your hands over her mouth and nose; and if she vomits because of it, all the better.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, he takes a pot and makes an opening in the lid, and puts in herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as wormwood, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water over fire; then he puts one end of a pipe into the pot and the other end into the mouth of the wound, and applies heat until the vapors enter the wound; then he makes her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then remove the pus gently.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this treatment and is not cured, he should command the midwife to moisten her left hand with oil of sesame or with musk-scented ointment, and then insert it into the birth canal, and search for the placenta; and when she has found it, she should grasp it and gently stretch it, little by little, so that the wound does not tear during extraction; but she must move it slightly from side to side, and then pull; it will come out.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the wound is constricted, we have spoken of the cure for sneezing, and of the fumigation of herbs; and if it is not cured by all that we have said, then beware of fooling around with it; but you should bind what is at the mouth of the wound to the thigh of the woman, then cauterize it with a tetrafarmacon ointment; then she will defecate and recover, and the foul odor will exit; but nevertheless, when she defecates, there comes a bad odor in the stomach and head, and the patient feels ill.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, you should use appropriate smoke: some of the ancients have tried smoke from watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one smokes out the woman for retained flowers and afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It is like glass in appearance, and the narrow end is put into nature, and the wide end is held over the fire; and the fumigation is applied to the charcoal, and the disease until it is cured, then another one is started.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born with an imperforate anus; their rectum is closed by a thin membrane. Therefore, the midwife should pierce this membrane with her finger, and not pierce it with a sharp instrument, and she must be careful not to touch the membrane with her fingernail; then she should apply soft lamb's wool soaked in wine and oil, and the wound will heal of itself.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will heal, then insert a peg of wooden splint and leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go in the chamber pot.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stopping of bleeding comes suddenly from a wound or an abscess; then it must be stopped suddenly: then it should be treated as we have said with the wooden splint.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula in ano
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come below the anus are nodules, and they grow larger when they originate from beneath the anus or in between its two parts, whether there is one fistula or several; and when this nodule becomes old, it opens up, and usually discharges a white or yellowish fluid, and sometimes they are suppurating; and they are caused by what comes out through either defecation or flatulence when the patient expels gas, and sometimes a worm comes out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that pierce all the way to the bladder, and halfway down the penis; and they reach the hip joint, and the scrotum.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula that flows in the anus and does not flow: and it is that you press your index finger or anus, and insert a thin needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no twist.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has tortuosity, insert a thin tent or horsehair until you feel the tent or hair in your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no emission of pus nor wind comes out as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; so hurry to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has reached the bladder or the urethra, and the urine escapes, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it has penetrated to the joint of the thigh, the tent will come out at the location; if there is no tortuosity and the source of the pain turns inward, then it will come out again, and neither medicine nor poultices by ointment will help; and in these flowing fistulas there is no cure except by hard work and the vanity of foolish physicians who interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that which is not persian and is not old, there is hope of health by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you lift his legs up to his thighs, and have his thighs inclined towards his belly; then insert a tent made of copper or lead if there is any tortuosity, as far as you know where the tent goes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must insert your index finger, unless of course the tent has pierced through; and let it be exposed where you feel between your finger and the flesh, then you know that it is persian; do not work on it otherwise if it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One nevertheless can still heal some, but that happens rarely; and the aid one does, is that one burns the cautery sutilly according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before; and one inserts it all hot into the fistula, as far as it comes out by the anus; and do this twice or thrice, until you know that these burned flesh are like a feather of a bird; and then cure it with wet tents soaked in butter, until those burned flesh come off, and then cure it with ointment smearing flesh and binding.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus without pain, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is thus without pain, that is good. If it does not otherwise heal; and if the tent pierces, and does not penetrate to the bone which is in the foundation, and there is between your finger and the tent a thick covering of flesh or of syphac, and you see the fistula near the covering of the heart; then cut off the beginning of the fistula, and pour in afterwards before the tent, and cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the chief of the tent; and the tent will be released, and fall out; then mend those flesh wounds that look like a bird's feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pus comes out, and flows between you and the wound, then cauterize it with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery gathers two things: namely, the burning of those flesh wounds, and the stanching of blood and the drying up of moisture; then the treatment of moist tents with butter or crushed substance, until the place where the fires burned in the bowels, and the wound heals over the arse; then treat the wound of the swelling veins with hard flesh, and they are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way to the fundament, and is distant from the body, put your finger into it, and probe it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and within it is the membrane or sac, or it is about to burst, there should be no fear but confidence and hope through one of three methods: either cauterize as we have said, or cut to the bottom, or if you can, insert a tent and cure as before; do not go too deep however, lest you cut into the structure supporting the bottom, and let the evacuation happen through that opening; then cure as we have said; it may be healed. Or remove that covering and clean after it is cut from below the sac, by tent or other pointed instrument; then cleanse the wounded tissue within the wound as much as possible; then try to restore the wound and dam the fistula in the affected area beyond the bottom: thus the patient will feel less discomfort.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes there are fistulas in this way; and when you put the tent into the fistula, it is on the side of the fundament near the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the top according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he inserts a twisted thread through it, and pushes the tent all along the thread into the fistula until it reaches its tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is bleeding inside the margin of the fundament, then pull out the thread from that hole so that you can put your finger into the fundament; and pull on the end of the thread and bring the two sides together and press them tight, and leave them for one or two days; and sometimes they need to be pressed until the threads cut through the flesh between them and the wound heals.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not drain, then have it drained in every way you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to cover the wound with a bandage so tightly, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spatumile (a tool used to create a fistula) is sharp on one side and smooth on the other; so that it doesn't cut what it shouldn't, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two types: either they are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and some discharge blood, and there may be one or more, and they are outside the anus and at the top of the anus; but those that are outside have little moisture, and sometimes a little citrine water or a little blood, and they have the color of the body. The treatment for those who have them inside the anus is to instruct the patient to straining while defecating until the veins break and the threads appear; then you hurry and grab it with tweezers, or hold it with your nail, then cut it at its roots; and if the nails cannot hold it because of moisture, they take it with a piece of cloth, or cotton, or a piece of camel's hair; and pull it out with their fingers, then cut it, and dust some hot powder on top that is used for cauterization; or you cauterize them as described in the chapter on cauterization, after treating other hemorrhoids until they are healed; and if the anus cannot come out, then the patient should be clistere with a sharp and harsh enema to clean what is inside the anus so that it can come out clearly. When the patient strains and the veins break through the anus, the treatment is easy; you grab them with your nail or tweezers, cut them, then treat them as we have said until they are healed and afraid of iron incision.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Take a twisted thread, and pierce it with a needle, then bring the thread to the top, and pierce the needle from the other side; turn both ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be loose; tighten the thread properly, then tie the thread, and take out the needle, and do likewise with all the others, and leave one to draw off the superfluity of blood; then place a moistened cloth in rose oil or cerate over the wound, and command the patient to rest; then let it be until it heals, and when it has healed, treat it with ointment and other remedies.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of dryness of the anus or rectum
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is dryness of the bowels due to constipation from natural causes, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you should cut the skin at the tip of a spatula or your nail, so that it does not get moist; then treat it until it is dry as it should be; and if it cannot dry, then restart the cutting more strongly than before, until it heals well and is peeled; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small appearance of freckles before the body, and they go very deeply; and sometimes the frost bites them, and one feels them as if dead with trembling, and they come throughout the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a candle made of goose fat, or a fat vulture feather, and place this candle on the trembling, so that the purple circle around the trembling; then return your hand to the entire candle so that you stroke all around the trembling, and push it deeply, and draw out the trembling by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you can, make a cane of brass or iron according to this shape, and let it be thin beneath and broad above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you can, cauterize the vein, as it is described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes an enema is made of silver or brass, or of molten and hammered copper; and sometimes they are made from these small and large instruments, according to those who use them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are used in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the enema, whether small or large, is placed on top, or the belly is bound in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And it has a bag of intestines that is tied, as you see, and the intestines are pierced inside; and it has two openings on one side, and one opening on the other; and the intestines where medicine is placed is made of a beast's bladder or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes, and there is an inch of space between each hole, then insert strong threads through these holes in a twisted pattern, and assemble the bag so that it resembles a goat; and when the medicine is inside, attach it to the instrument with a strong thread, then catheterize; and this is the shape of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with oil or egg white, or something similar, then insert it gently; then press the minister's hands together on the tube until it is all used up, then remove the tube, and let the patient lie with his legs against the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him squint as much as he can; and if he sleeps for a night afterward, that is a great help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you catheterize him for diarrhea, and the medicine rushes to come out, then he should be given more until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the rectum or anus, the tube should be as thin as for a child; and this is the shape of the thin tube which presses against the skin:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken of wound treatment in the section on surgery; now we will speak of treatments using hands and medicine, according to the situation.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and according to what makes them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by stone, and cutting with sword and knife, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar objects; or they are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or head, or leg, or abdomen, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because their memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a stone or similar object, and the skin is still broken and the wound is large, and you quickly doubt a hot abscess: then immediately make a tourniquet using the cephalic vein itself if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the tourniquet be on the opposite side of the injured part; and keep the patient free from wine and rich foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.
