And if he does not want to tourniquet, then reduce his food intake, and do not drink wine or eat meat; and put on the wound, if hot abscesses come out, cotton wet only in rose oil, or in stippressive wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by the air, powder that I will describe a little later; and if the burn has been moved by the air, then put on some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that from a sword, and the lips cannot be brought together with stitches, then bring them together with a ligature, as I will describe for abdominal wounds.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and it can be seen, and only hangs on by a bit, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as testicles and cooked wheat, also like fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rot in the skin, and it does not reach to the bone, then cut away the rotten flesh, and gouge it out, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which bleeds profusely, and cannot be staunched by medicine, then tie off the artery, and if that doesn't help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy; you should put this powder on so that it burns until the pain has subsided.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is thus: take one part incense; two parts dragon's blood; three parts quicklime, and powder it finely, and employ it upon the wound, and bind it firmly, until it heals well and joins to all its flesh; and then dress it well, and leave it without removing it, if it does not swell; for they do not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one should only cauterize with chalk, when they don't have incense or dragon's blood, but as long as the cautery moves the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the burn has moved the wound, let it be in the same state, and do not put any of this powder on it; but apply some digestive ointments, or barley flour made with water and honey, until it becomes soft; then cure it with other cures until it heals.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	If a bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, I will extract it with subtle pincers; and I will tell you about fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	of a wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is single, there is no difference between it and one on the head, but if the nerves of the neck or arteries are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, do not apply any restraining cure, for it harms the nerves and makes them withdraw; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but use moist medicines, such as hot water washed in cool water, and cooked honey mixed with rose oil, and also washed cooked stone, and other minerals according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cut it and bind it, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is chapped and full of pus, then pierce it or a lower place; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding ensues, then stop it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the carotid, and the passage for food is blocked, causing the flesh to sink in, then cut the skin above the windpipe on the neck, and do not touch the windpipe but reset it according to its natural shape; and then bind it up gently, and leave it for several days, then treat it with poultices until it heals; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then trepan it; and if there are pieces of bone, then draw them all out if you can, and those that you cannot reach, leave them until the wound heels over and the wound is cleaned and the passage unblocked; and if the wound is fresh, then use the powder I have described.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have described in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then examine whether the wound bleeds profusely: thus you will know that the wound is mortal; but if it is not deep, and the wound is fresh with all its blood, then do not put the powder in during the first hour, nor ligature it for the bleeding that may emerge from the depth, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you do not have an ointment, then place old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and let the patient sleep with his head on the wound for three, four or more days; thus no spasms, nor evil tremors of the heart, nor strangulations of the intestines will come; and when you see good dispositions, then you know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure it with tenting and other remedies until it heals; and if it cannot heal, and there is still a wound, then you know there is a fistula; so treat it as it should be treated.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is simple, in the front or back, treat it as above; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, poweder it, and if it is deep in the bone, and has torn pieces, then clean the wound and draw out the foreign objects; and for other wounds in other parts of the body, judge as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	There are great, medium and small ruptures of the belly; from a large wound sometimes the intestine, or the nerves of the intestines, protrude, which causes the passage of air; and stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because one must stitch up the intestines little by little, warming them gradually as one does so; because the intestines swell as soon as they feel cold, and they are more difficult to stitch up. And know that there are four types of ruptures in the belly: the two common sutures occur in stitching the belly, and the sutures of other wounds in the body; and the other two own sutures are common to other wounds, although they are more appropriate with the belly, and I will describe each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestine has come out, and there is something to be put back, it can be done in one of two ways: either due to the size of the wound as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen with cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in such a way: moisten a sponge or soft cloth in lukewarm water only, or cook in squinant water with cypress and spike, and warm the intestine until the swelling is gone; and sometimes this wine restringent is made, and it is used alone to reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling go down, moisten the intestine with water or altus and mallows that have been cooked, for this constricts the opening a little; and if it cannot be inserted, then make a small hole in the wound with an instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and the first cure is better than cutting, which one should not do without great need; and the instrument for splitting it is: insert it into the fold and push it out, and see the form here:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines burst out, he should be sewn up again according to their natural form in its proper place, if you have the power, for this is best.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and it is in the lower belly, you should make the patient lie on his back with his legs above his head; and if it is in the upper abdomen, he should be placed so that his head and feet are higher than his torso, and likewise if the rupture in the belly is to one side, then he should be positioned so that the wounded part is higher than the other; and thus you should arrange matters as I say for both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds take what is appropriate for the task; then hold in your hand an instrument with which you push together the edges of the wound, and this is how you should sew: pierce both sides of the skin and the underlying muscle with a needle and strong thread tied to it; pull the needle through so that it comes out on the other side, leaving a loop of thread; then bring the two edges of the wound together and tie the ends of the thread in a knot; leave an interval between each stitch equal to half a finger; use needles that are not too small or thick, for the thin ones tear the flesh and the thick ones do not pierce it well; then tie off the loops of thread so that they do not hurt the patient when he sleeps, and put tents or bandages over the needles to hold them in place until the wound is healed; this method of sewing with needles is best for small wounds. The second kind of sewing is common, and it involves pushing together both sides of the skin and underlying muscle with a needle and strong thread tied to it; once you have passed the needle through all four layers, bring it back up where you started, as one would sew a garment, leaving an interval between each stitch equal to half a finger; this sewing method is suitable for large wounds. I sewed up a wound on a man's belly that had been cut with a knife; the wound was more than a palm in width and the intestines protruded two palms out of it; the wound was in the middle of his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned his entrails after he had been dead for 24 hours, and the wound was sewn up for 15 days, and I healed him, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they had judged him to be dead, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where there was no medicine to be found, nor any other remedies; and I placed old cotton on the wound twice daily, and washed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you about two proper methods of sewing: take the needle, and pierce it from the outside through to the inside; when it has pierced the skin directly through, hold the thread where it emerges on the other side, and pierce it again from the inside out, so that the needle emerges on the other side. The understanding of this stitching is that you sew as a tailor sews pelts, and you leave the thread hanging on one side, then grab and pull it through to the other, until the seam is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, which Galen describes correctly, is like joining two pieces of cloth together naturally, and applying one end of the thread to the other, in such a way: insert a needle at the top of the wound near the edge, and pierce that spot only, leaving the two ends of the wound; then turn the needle and pierce from the outside in, to the inside, through the two ends of the wound; then pierce one and then the other from the outside in, through two other points on the skin near the edge of the wound; and this is the best and most common method of sewing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this, and some testify to it: one should sew the belly with two needles, with thread in each; and one should push one needle in from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew up sores; and know that when the rut is in the middle of the belly, the sewing is more difficult than in other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are like the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound full of blood, as long as the burn has not moved, then put back the intestines and the gut; then put on the powder-charcoal, and if the burn has not moved, put on any ointment available until the wound heals; then sew up the wound with silk thread, and solder the sutures, and the mirach; then cure the wound as with others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicine, put on old cotton, as soon as it starts to heal, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you don't need any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound might cause gangrene in the principal limbs, then moisten a light blanket in warm tempered oil, or rose oil, and place it around the angles, and under the armpits; and if there is pain or swelling in the bowels, and it happens many times, then enema with warm black wine, and likewise if the swelling reaches the intestines; and perforate it from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines, which are called 'young', cannot heal when they are raw, and this is due to the thinness of their walls, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and their proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the skin around the wound tears, reset it as one would reset the intestines while it is still fresh; but if it has become green or black, tie up the area that is black so that no blood flow returns to it, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut away what is between the stitch, and hang the two edges of the wound above the wound itself until it eases to aid extraction when the sutures come out, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the road of boiling
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are ruptured and the wound is small, it can sometimes be cured in some people, for I saw a man who was stabbed in the belly with a lance; the wound was on the right side of his stomach, and it became inflamed and formed into an abscess, from which he passed both stool and wind; I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not cease to apply poultices until it healed and the edges came together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewing it up, I feared that the patient had a problem in his belly; and he had no harm but stayed in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in such a way: take a thread from a large testicle, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened the mouth, put it on the two lips so that it holds his mouth shut; and then tie the head, and it will stay so that he cannot undo it; then put another thread after in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed; and cauterize the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the wound is in the intestine and the patient suffers no harm, one can sew up the intestine with a fine thread cut from an animal's intestine, in this way: take the end of the intestinal thread which is well-charred, and then tie to it a fine linen thread twisted, then thread it through the needle and stitch the intestine, and draw it together; and this manner of stitching with threads offers no certainty except according to the way of hope and expectation; and if the wound is large and broad, especially when it is in one of the grails of the intestine, there is no healing except by subtle means.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it wakes up, is universally called a "fistula", and especially when it is swollen and becomes bowed inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And the fistula is according to its appearance, a hard, white nodule without pain, and it is bowed like the beak of a bird; sometimes it is clear and bowed, and sometimes thick; sometimes small, and sometimes large enough; I have already spoken about these in the division of wounds that any wound which is not healed and has no matter, is only due to one of nine causes: that is, because of the weakness of blood or body; or because of its evil nature; or because there is hard matter within it, and on the surface, which does not allow matter to emerge; or there is too much inflammation; or the location is damaged, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good for treatment; or because the corruption has a pestilential nature; or because the digestion and recovery in that region are slow by nature, and it is swollen. And I have already shown all these causes and their signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I will tell you about the treatment of a fistula that is done by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins and arteries and nerves, from the face, or the bowels, or the bladder, or any of the sides, or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and also to any part that comes to the principal member, and in similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this way are very painful to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the places I have mentioned, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it being understood, then take a tent of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, so hold it; and if the fistula is crooked, then search with a slender tent of lead, for the lead bends easily around the crookedness; and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot well probe it with tents, then cleanse it through one of the openings by enema, for moisture moves from one opening to another, and cleanses; then squeeze it hard as you can, so that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and feel how deep it goes, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press your hand, and where he feels it most; and when you truly know the location, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or in any of the places I have mentioned, then treat it as I have instructed, and remove the foulness and corrupted matter within; then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep and straight, you should probe deeply as much as you can, then put moist tents in medical water, and insert them into the fistula up to its head, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; then apply healing ointments to soft flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is damaged by the fistula, treat it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve troubles the principal limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then treat it with a king's touch until the corruption is completely removed, then cure it with things that warm it until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns to its previous state, know that you have not gone deep enough: uncover and probe until you reach the bottom, remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is healed in this way, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; then let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupt bone, and you can pull it out with tweezers, then extract it with the appropriate instrument for this purpose, and if there are many bones, draw them all out, leaving none behind; and if moisture causes contrary effects, and there is no error or fear, then cut and dry and warm, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place something on the wound to encourage pus to flow, and let it remain until the pus has gathered around the bone, and then the bones will come apart more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, then clean only the rottenness until all the blackness is removed, then close up the wound; and if there is a great deal of corruption, and it extends to the soft tissue of the bone, then it must be cleaned and packed all the way to the corruption, and then the wound treated until it is healed. And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take example and help from this in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of about 30 years who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that matter came to the leg and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it; but the doctors, through their folly, worked on it until the abscess opened and much matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many openings appeared from which pus and fluid from the body flowed; and many doctors treated him for 2 years, and there was no one skilled in the art of medicine, so that I was called to see him, and I saw his leg and the remedies with which he was being treated, and what flowed from the openings into a great wound; and the skin of the young man became red and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent at one of the openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that some came up against each other from different parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried, therefore, and probed one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, which I found to be corrupt and pierced, the corruption extending into the bone; I cut away what appeared to me to be of the corrupt bone, believing that there was no more corruption except what I removed; and then I began to dress the wound with strong remedies for a long time, but could not heal it; so I began again, and discovered the bone as before, finding the corruption still continued in the bone; I cut it away, and then removed it, and strove to heal the place; but I was unable to probe more than a palm's breadth of the bone, and had to abandon it for the time being, on account of the weakness of the patient who could not bear any longer, and also from fear of death, which I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often because of the bloody evacuation he suffered, but was completely healed, and in the place of the bone a hard lump grew, and he had a good disposition and no harm or contrary effect at all, neither walking nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, it should be bound in this way: take a bandage and tighten it at the head of the open bone, and order someone to raise it upwards; and put another larger woolen bandage over the hard lump that is above the bone, and bind the head, so that you pull the corrupted flesh underneath, and uncover the flesh on top of the place where you see there should be binding, so that the bandage does not press on the flesh; and put a fire or a board under the bone to cover the corrupted flesh; and one should bind as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and bind again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the bone is broken and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then expose the flesh all around; then put a fire under it, and then draw out the corruption from one side to the other, and make the incision close to the site of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and bind the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other way to treat it except to cut; and if the corruption is at the knuckle of the hand or the foot, this is a very serious matter, but nonetheless you must investigate the corrosion, how it presents itself to you; and cleanse it in every way that you can, but be careful not to harm the vein or nerve; and know that there are many ways to cut and bind these bones, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance, their thickness and thinness, their size and smallness, and their hardness. And therefore one must prepare a tool for each type of work; and know that the work will show you the tool that you will need, according to your knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of illnesses; and then choose the tool that you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The heads can be injured either internally or externally; and when you have treated this injury with remedies, and they are not effective, then cover the affected limb up to the point where the injury occurs, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater harm, by the defect in the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, as if burned by fire, and after the blackness there is swelling, then this corruption spreads from limb to limb, and throughout the body; so act quickly in covering it up, and if the injury is caused by the sting of some venomous creature, such as a sea scorpion or adder or similar, and the injury is on the head, then cover it, and give no space for the venom to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if the injury reaches the hand, then cover it at the joint so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, then cover it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that is death, and there is no remedy that can be applied beyond what its nature permits; and do likewise when the injury is on the foot: if it reaches the first joint, then cover after the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, then cover the whole foot; and if it ascends into the leg, then cover at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no remedy for this injury except to tie the limb from below and from above, and extend one instrument down the ligature, and another minister up the other ligature, and you separate the flesh that is between the two ligatures with a spatulum as wide as the wound, so that the bone is exposed; then cover it and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the ligature does not touch the healthy area, and this prevents further injury and abscesses.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the area gently, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his sleep: he had a blackness that looked like a burn, and this corrosion began first on his toe of the foot, so that it affected the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he bandaged his foot, and was healed; and long afterwards the corrosion returned to his finger, and he came to me, and I applied repulsive substances after purification of the body, and he could not stop the corrosions; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to do it, for I had no hope that it would repel the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the man's vitality was weak; and he became desperate, returned to his home, and bandaged his hand, and was healed; and I have not heard of anyone else doing this, except for those who need it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	At times an abscess forms in a fleshy part, and remains so long that it causes a large gathering of pus; and then they burst and pierce, and the pus leaks out, leaving the place hollow like a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as a piece of cloth, and does not heal over to the bone or nerve, and such a disease is called 'sore', and not 'fistula'; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone all around, then it is called a 'fistula'; and the skin is such that you can cover it all around, and especially when it is thin, like a piece of cloth; and it does not heal over.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have confidence that the skin is healing and the corruption is not deep, and the flesh is thick, then treat it with a clyster thus: examine if the breast is swollen, and the pus that comes from it has a foul odor, then prepare an Egyptian medicine as follows: take equal parts of ash, oil, and litarge, and put it in a vessel over fire, until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take some according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and clysterize the breast, and compress the orifice; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then express it out; do this many times, until the breast is clean and the pus is removed; and sometimes one is clysterized with ashes of vine wood, when this medicine is not available, and it is done thus: take vine wood ashes, and pour water over them, then strain it and clysterize with it, until you see that the breast is clean; and if the patient cannot bear it, or the Egyptian medicine, then use water and honey with a little litarge ground in it; or clysterize with honey and wine, so that the honey cleanses and washes, and the wine dries up the sore; and when you have done this, and are confident that the breast is clean, then clysterize it with something that produces flesh inside it, and take diaphoretic plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or clysterize with other medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken in the section on ointments; and if the opening to the breast is small, and the tip of the clyster cannot enter, then enlarge it a little with a needle, and apply some Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged enough; and if the wound is too large, then cut it and leave only the place where the clyster can enter, and if the opening that drains the pus is above, then cover it higher up, or lower down according to where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Because when the bowels are in pain, you should not let any food in and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, then arrange it so that the bowels move to the lowest place they can; and when the bowels are in pain, do not let any food in and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, then arrange it so that the bowels move slightly downward, and leave nothing of the bowels behind; take consolidating medicines to put over the wound, and have them above the linen drape that covers the entire wound; then cover the most forceable spot on the breast, making the hole larger than before, then apply a soothing ointment on the other drape according to the size of the hole, and place it over the wound to lighten the bowels, and do not remove the large drape for several days at a time; and the one that is over the wound, remove often to remove the bowels, and know what comes from the bowels, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and see if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature that rises on the wound, then know that the breast has healed and is approaching health; and then loosen it in the morning, or midday, and when you loosen the wound, change the other drape and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast milk flows for many days, know that the breast will not dry up.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons run long, do not despair of health, for health is near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	There are people whose wounds fester for a long time with putrid flesh, and those who have the opposite condition; and if indigestible food sits in the belly after many days, know that the belly is not healing; and if the belly takes a long time to heal and is swollen, then use drying medicines that are moist in substance but dry in nature, like diaphanous ointment, for it contains a great deal of vitriol, and it is the best medicine. Take diaphanous ointment, and make it with rose oil, and rose water equal in substance; then cook it and use it. And the same is done with thickened honey when diaphanous ointments are not available; take myrrh, aloes, and incense, and grind them into powder over the honey while it is on the fire; then glue a cloth to it, and place it on the belly, and sometimes one administers aristologus root, which is like flour made from beans and centaury; and use simples or compounds: grind them into powder and mix with the honey I mentioned, and use it. And if the cure is drawn out and not healed by this cure, then know that corruption has gone deep, and it makes impressions in the bone, or in the hard parts, or in the soft tissues; then use the fistula cure, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaritis is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or occasionally in other digits; and when it becomes inflamed, and no attention is paid to it, then it develops into a hard abscess, and it runs and seeps down to the root of the nail, and sometimes all the way to the bone; and corrosion sets in right down to the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the digit becomes swollen, and the colour turns purple.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the section on treatment, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the surplus nail that remains, and then cauterise the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cautery is a great help if the bone and nail are sound; and if the nail grows over the flesh, and begins to press on it, and the nail becomes ingrown, then you must place a thread beneath the nail so that the flesh can grow out from under the nail, and draw the thread up, and cut away the flesh carefully and gently, and apply burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything; then treat with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and pull it out, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see the finger is corrupted, cut it at the first joint of the fingernail, as has been said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is frostbitten and swollen, and causes great pain, then you must heal it first; then cut the nail of the finger at an angle from the side, and be careful that the cutting does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, place something over it to soothe the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two types of fingernails that grow on the hands of some men by chance are all flesh, and by chance they have bones, and sometimes they have nails, and sometimes they grow at the base of the joint, or the growth is in some fingers of the hand.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those born in the webbing of the finger do not move, but those born at the joint of the finger may move; the size of one who is fleshy is thus: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; therefore, keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one who is born in the webbing of the finger, you must first cut the flesh around the bone to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate thread, then treat it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joint dislocations that come together come from birth, or from the dislocation of a wound, or from burns, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Then you must cut the suture, so that the fingers grow according to their natural shape; then put between two swabs or damp cloths in rose oil, so that they do not stick together; or you put between two pieces of thin plank, until the sewings are healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If this occurs in one of his hands with the palm, then treat that fracture as it should be treated.
des vils	of the vile
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Wens are large, enveloped, swollen veins full of melancholy humors that come in many parts of the body; and they occur more in legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him a purgative drink made from woad, and then give him the basil-based remedy.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with fire is according to two methods: one is that you cut it, and draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you raise the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done in this way: first, raise the leg with very hot water until the large veins are dilated, then stretch the leg from the thigh to just below the knee; then make an incision, one, two, or three inches long, in one place, and draw out the black blood with your hand from one end to the other, as much as the virtue of the medicine can bear; then ligature it, and command that he eat foods causing constipation while taking black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and do not harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the disease is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair on it, then put it in a bath and warm the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it over a fire, and then press down on the vein near the knee or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin at the edge of the vein, and scrape the vein from both sides until it bleeds when touched; and when it is seen to be red and black, and when it sinks into the skin it looks like a white cord; then pierce the vein under the skin with a needle, and tie and draw it, and pierce another vein below, and repeat this three times; then scrape the skin over the vein until it bleeds, then release it at one end, and tie and draw it, and pierce another vein above, as before; then pierce another vein, or several if necessary, then release and pierce at the toe, then draw and release to the second piercing; then draw it out from vein to vein until it is completely extracted, then press on it; and if you cannot draw and raise it, pierce a needle through it with strong double thread, tie and draw it, and pierce under the vein, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out; and be careful not to pierce it, for if it is pierced, it cannot be drawn or raised, and the patient will suffer harm; and when you have completely treated it, place moist wool soaked in wine and rose oil over the wound site, and dress it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it twistsly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one covers a vein is curved and does not cut so that it covers the vein; and it is of great curvature because if it were thin, it would cover the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of a civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is bent in the legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in land where there is no moisture; and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the pus that comes under the skin, just as snakes and worms come inside the body, bent between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a great inflammation comes in the leg, then the place changes color, and the vein begins to come out, as does the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, you must wrap around it a piece of woolen cloth about two and a half inches to three inches in width, and tie it, leaving the cloth hanging on the leg, and every time something comes out from inside, wrap the remaining cloth around, and do not cover it at its root as long as it is all coming out; because if you cover it, it will return into the body, and will bring about an abscess and swelling in that place, for which reason this thing should be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing of it should remain in the body; and sometimes this vein is as long as five or ten palms, and a man came to me once whose was twenty palms long, and when you cover it, you must plug the hole with a straw, and pierce it to the bottom so that everything comes out, and empty out the matter inside which is causing the issue, and apply healing medicines in that place for a few days, then treat it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein bleeds profusely, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or in the foot, and a lot of pus comes out, and from which it rains; therefore, treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "cow disease" in our land because it often affects cows, and it is caused by a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, traveling throughout the body, ascending and descending, until it breaks through the skin, and it can enter the eye and destroy it; this happens quite frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and treated, you cannot prevent it from emerging when it appears: therefore, you must tie the area above and below tightly with a strong string, then cut it out, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh, cauterize it with fire until it dies; its greatest harm is that it can affect the eye as we have said, so if you see it approaching the eye, squeeze it firmly from underneath, then cut it out.
