The patient should also be cleansed with medicated lotions to remove putrid humors, and given purgative foods to reduce the proliferation of noxious humors.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vomiting" in our language, and it is a pain that affects some members, and then moves from one member to another; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of the arm; and then soon after, I saw it rise up onto the shoulder like a worm, quickly, as quickly as silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain left that spot and settled in the shoulder, and then a little later spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it was circling around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered a lot how she moved from limb to limb like this, because I had never seen this disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I have seen many people whose pain moved from one place to another, but I have not seen it as I did in the woman; and I thought that it was because women have dry bodies, and their veins are exposed, and this forced the flatulence to appear; and this is not apparent according to this reason in those who are delicate, and whose bodies are moist and their veins relaxed.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then bind it above and below tightly, and then press on it until that windiness is forced out of its place; and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it yourself, then treat it with that which expels windiness, such as foul pills, and pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, depending on their appearance and depending on where in the body they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their heads is that there are some with large points, and small, and barbed, and smooth; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and those which pierce into any limb pierce in two ways: either into a principal limb, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestine, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls therefore in any part of the members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you hereafter, appears to you: then you must beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not imbedded deeply, then pull it out, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain is when the arrow pierces the bone and penetrates the brain, and if there is bleeding from the wound which is on the brain, and if there is a fever and swelling and redness in themselves, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and disturbance of the mind, and vomiting of phlegm; and perhaps there is also discharge from the nose or ears; and perhaps they lose their speech and voice; and from the wound there is white moisture like pus, and it also oozes out like blood; and if this sign appears to you, then cease the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it has not entered deeply.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the seizure when it affects the heart are that it is on the left side of the chest, and feels as if it were stuck in a hard object, not moving; and sometimes the seizure causes muteness like the apoplexy, and black blood comes out, and there is chilliness and cold sweat, and syncope: then know without doubt that death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the arrow that never leaves the lung are: spitting up foam without pain, and a swollen throat, and the patient changes color, and breathes hard and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow hits in the skin of the foot, it is among the small bones; and it causes great pain and great swelling and breathlessness; and all the limbs from the shoulders are affected.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, perhaps something indigestible will come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces the gut and feces escape through the intestines, then there is no hope for a cure or for removing the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces the bladder and urine escapes and flows out, and the patient feels great pain: know that this wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and armpit and spine of the back and hip and thigh and legs, and similar members, are safe according to several dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you to do, so that you can do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	A certain person had a seizure and it struck the jaw at the root of the nose; I treated it by pressing on it and then releasing it under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without any numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And on a child I treated a seizure that struck the fatty tissue under the eye below the eyelid, and the seizure was repelled, and only the tip could be touched towards the root of the nose; the seizure was as large as a Turkish arrowhead, all iron-colored without ears; the child was healed and no ill effects occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic, with ears: I cut the beards, and delicately extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I extracted an arrow from a man who had it lodged in his throat, and I thought he would die; and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not improve; so I cut into the arrow, and dislodged it, and pulled it out, and he suffered no ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a person with an arrow lodged in his back, and the wound is sewn up over it; and the arrow remains inside him, and his natural functions are unaffected, and he suffers no harm in any of his natural processes.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man who had an arrow lodged in his face, and the wound was sewn up; and it remained there without causing him great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated an arrow wound in the head of a prince who had a arrow stuck in his eye, and it was slightly inclined to the right; and the arrow was all swollen. I was called to attend him after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it with a thin instrument, and did not feel anything; but he felt pain and pressure below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I applied a digestive and astringent poultice to the site, so that the swelling would go down; and I could see the head of the arrow.Et la dis je qu’il fust sainz, si li leus de la saiette estoit hors del leu, et si ne i demourast mie pointure ne dolor; car li leus enflast et s’alarga a tous costez.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the ointment many times, and healed the wound directly, and the patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound many times, until it was opened, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow which was lodged in the wound; then I adjusted the opening of the wound with the medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly; and the patient recovered well within four months, and then the wound healed so that I could not extract the arrow; therefore I did not cease to use instruments and tricks, until one day I took the arrow with some good tweezers, according to the form which will be described at the end of this chapter, and I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; I restored it therefore, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I will tell you of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you may apply my treatment to anything else which I do not mention, for books cannot encompass everything; but wise masters often discover something new from little things, and from what is present and defective, they find a new cure, and a new instrument, in the case of strange diseases which occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows enter the body in two ways, either through the place where they strike, or through another part; and those which go straight in through the spot where they strike are called arrow-wounds through flesh, and these sometimes heal up now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, let it be left until the swelling around the wound has gone down and the opening has healed; and if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for a few days, moving it every day; and then it will come out, and if it does not, pierce all around with a very thin needle until the opening is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the skull, and goes right through to one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the aforementioned symptoms appear: do not remove it, but leave it until it is even after a few days, for if the arrow reaches the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck in the brain, and does not reach the brain, and the patient survives for a few days without any bad symptoms, then use this method to remove it:
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deep and cannot be extracted, then treat around it as I have told you; then heal the area until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in the body where it cannot be seen, then seek it throughout the entire body; and if you feel it, then draw it out with a suitable instrument; and if due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then cut around the wound as much as necessary for the wound to be large enough; and draw out the arrow if you can, and if there are ears by which it is attached, remove the flesh that is pierced on both sides as far as you can, and then break or fold over the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow as you pull it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then leave it until around the area it entered is swollen, then milk it, for extraction is easier then.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding causes a contrary effect, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of cutting into nerves and opening veins, and use any means you can to gently pull out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient in the position he was in when the arrow hit him, for that is the greatest help, and if you cannot, then position him according to what the symptoms show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, or where something appears from it, or the skin is swollen in such a place that one sees or feels it apparently: cut above it, as far as the pincers can grasp, and then pull it out; thus jump out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then rotate your hand rapidly so that it goes into the bone and widens the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it cannot come out, then leave it for now and try to extract it again until it comes out; if there is a fragment of the arrow, then insert the instrument all the way in; and if the shaft is broken and you see that you can apply pressure, then press the instrument into the broken shaft so that the point of the arrow goes into the instrument's hole; then pull it out, and if the arrow is stuck in the instrument, then pull the instrument in with the point going in, to make the extraction easier.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisonous, then you must cut off all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, and then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow pierces the leg or foot or belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close by, and you can cover it up if it is struck; and be careful not to cover the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then dress the wound, if necessary; and cure it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to treat arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the feathered end [of the arrow] is also like the feathers on an bird, to push against the tip of the arrow, just as it is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of tongs for prying and probing is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins in the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which one can bleed, and there are sixteen in the head, namely: two batons located behind the ears, called 'ear-beaks'; and two arteries in the temples that are visible; and two veins in the corners of the eyes, called 'aspires'; and the vein in the middle of the forehead; and the vein at the top of the nose; and two windpipes located in the neck; and two veins above the lips, these are the veins called 'augerich'; and two veins under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which we commonly bleed are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, which is on the left side of the chest, and the common people call it 'vein of the head'; and the middle one is called 'fast', and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and the common people call it 'vein of the heart'; and the basilic is on the right side of the chest, and the common people call it 'vein of the belly', and it is above the hipbone, and it is that one from which we bleed, which opens clearly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein which is between the auricular and annular, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the curve of the pouch on the left side of the chest, and the second is sophene, which is at the ankle on the right side of the chest; and the vein called 'nesse', which is at the ankle on the other side.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of veins that are behind the ears is helped by old catarrh remedies and by emigrant; and the qualities of the bloodletting instrument, as I told you, and it is that you move the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then squeeze the patient's neck with a cloth until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head: then press them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, sign it with ink; then take the lance, and pierce it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand to the entire vein upstream, and pierce through the skin and the vein well with two strokes of the knife, and make the blood come out until you see it; then stop and ligate it, until it is healed; and I have already said about incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is good for old migraines, and for a headache, and for habitual ophthalmia, and for the body of tears ague to the eyes; and the qualities of the bleeding are as I said: and it is that the patient stretches his neck, so that the two veins appear clearly; and feel the pulse under your thumb, and then sign with your finger; then lift the vein above your thumb, and insert the lance below, and lift the vein above, and cup it, as you have done in the other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then bind it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their binding and their extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein in the forehead is as good as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for old diseases of the face, and for emigration and redness; and the qualities are such that the patient turns his neck in twisting until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "digging", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the amount you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed, and sometimes the work can be done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too sharp; and the wound is oblique, for the bone is close by, and perhaps the flame will break when it is very thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the temples helps with itches, and with tics, and with redness, and with eye orbs, and with facial diseases; and the qualities of their bleeding are such that the patient turns his neck in twisting, as before; then bleed them, and the bleeding should be through a small hole, with a wide flame, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the veins are subtle, perhaps they will break; then draw blood, as much as you need, and then ligature it with a thread, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein of the nose is useful for ague, and for sudden madness, and for facial diseases such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is chronic. The nature of this bleeding is that the patient holds his head, then squeezes his nostrils with his left hand, and takes a long, thin flame, and inserts it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well otherwise, and the blood will begin to flow now; do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then ligate it overnight, for it is quickly restored. And this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of the two sinuses helps with the constriction of the eyes, and with many diseases, and with itching, and with scabs, and with herpes, and with ulcers; and the nature of this bleeding is as we have said: the patient should hold his head down, and the doctor standing above him, then bleed the vein of the long one quite widely, then draw the blood temperately, or as much as is needed; then do the same in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and gently constrict both veins so that the patient does not choke; and leave it until the morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	on bleeding from the gums
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of veins in the lips above helps with sores in the mouth, and腐敗of gums, and splitting of lips, and pain in the teeth and gums.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of bleeding is to have the patient sit before you and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the lip and look at two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which can be recognized because they are black and because there are tiny black veins around them: compress both of them, and if you cannot distinguish them and you doubt their location, then compress the largest one on each side, and also do the same for the two veins above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	on bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of veins that are beneath the tongue is helped by the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is by the constriction of the throat, and by diseases of the uvula, and by diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the bleeding should be such that the patient holds the hand in front of the sun, and touches the tongue, and looks underneath each side to see a black vein: therefore heal one and then the other, and do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck from which one usually bleeds are bled in two ways: either with a wide silver pin, or an olive-wood point as thin as a toothpick, and is called "anesil"; and they are wide and thin according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the olive wood point is very renowned, and it is wide as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the smooth veins of the neck that contain thick and turbid blood, and that is the shape of the olive-wood point.And for opening the veins in the face, one must open those that are plain and contain thick blood; and it is a matter of skill to know which ones these are:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and subtle, used for bleeding the subtle veins where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The sanctuary of St. Basil, which is one of these veins, helps ailments that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleeding it, and to cauterize the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it hits the artery, and bleeding occurs, then it must be staunched as I have said; but the flame should not be clamped, but cut like a thread.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if St. Basil's vein does not open clearly, then you should move it and change to another; or you can cut a branch from it, or open the vein in the arm instead of it: it will open clearly; and then cauterize it with the flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the location of the opening, then you should stretch out the arm, and feel the pulse until you recognize it; then mark the spot on the inside, and then bind the arm, and cauterize the vein with the flame, as we have said; and be careful not to pierce the artery when you see the spot swollen, for that is the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it flow upwards like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood: therefore hasten and place your finger over it for a long time, then remove your finger if the flow stops, as often happens; tie up the arm and leave it thus, and do not move it until it has healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not staunched and it flows, and medicine is not present, then seize the artery and open it, for that is where the blood retreats; and staunch the flow.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of a fig tree, cut it in half, and take one half and tie it on firmly until the next day; if the flow of blood stops, that is good; if not, then stop it with one of the powders which stops bleeding, as we have said; but stopping the flow of blood is not easy in many cases because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The wound in the middle if it is bleeding from both above and below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the surgeon must be careful of the nerve underneath, and not cut too deeply, and find the nerve, which may be swollen and the nerve affected, and perhaps unable to heal; and this nerve often opens, and if it does not open in some men because of its subtlety, then you should treat it with an anaesthetic instrument; and guard the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, they cut it deeply.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The healing of the cephalic vein helps to draw blood from the head and aids the eyes; it should be healed by cauterizing with an olive-oil flame or a myrtle-oil flame, for this is the safest of all veins to cauterize as there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, one should seek the easiest place, and if it fails the first time, try again; and sometimes the site swells in some men when it fails the first time, but it does not cause any harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about healing is that it is only done to maintain health and prevent future illnesses; healing should be performed through one of the three veins: the cephalic, the fast, or the basilic; healing should be performed on the first day, or the third after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bleeding that is administered for illnesses does not have a determined time, but when there is a need during the day or night, at all times and in all seasons; and one should not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman who is pregnant beyond the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the very old who have passed 60 years be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when one wishes to bleed, in any manner, it is necessary to cleanse the intestines with a gentle clyster if he has much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw harmful excess fluids from the intestines towards the principal limbs; nor should one bleed those who are bloated from too much meat and wine, or those who are drunk, as long as they are so, nor those who are hydroptic. And one should not bleed after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, and excessive sexual intercourse with a woman, and from exertion, watching, fasting, and what depletes the body, either through an instrument or from the body; then subtly alter the humors, if the pulse is strong, through food, drink, and medicine, if you have the skill. Then enter the bath, if nothing hinders it, to subtly alter the blood, and bleed from the vein on the arm towards the elbow, as we have said, and be careful that day to avoid exertion, pricking, and lust, and similar things; and be calm and cheerful, and let the person bleeding be higher than the one being bled, and rub the arm two or three times, then tighten the ligature above the vein moderately, for if it is too tight or too loose, it will not affect the blood. Then wet the blade of the bleeding knife with a little old oil, then place his left index finger on that vein below where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not shrink and fail under the knife.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flow like cords to the armpit, and some that are filled with wind, so that when one applies flame, it retreats from the flame, and cannot open the vein; and so one must be careful of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; if not, he should try again a little lower on the same spot or above it, if the area is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the area is swollen and the patient is afraid, leave it for one or two days without binding the arm: perhaps a hot abscess will develop. Do not enter the bath, then restart the bleeding if she wishes; and if the opening is small, cut the skin around it subtly, and you doubt that it won’t release as much blood as you want, then apply the flame directly to that opening; and work it gently, so that the area is swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the spot is swollen, do not re-bandage the wound, but put a little liniment of oil there, for it lightens the body of blood, and in that place the liniment of oil is rendered; and thus administer the liniment of oil in every wound that you bandage veins to stop the flow of blood; and this also makes a blister and draws fluid out when applied to the spot; it disperses the blood when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, especially when it has not been bandaged before except for the small opening of the vein, then hurry and put a sponge soaked in warm water on the spot, and press for an hour; and you must do this after the flow of blood from the wound, and if there is any darkness or greenness remaining on the spot afterwards, it does not hurt; and if you see it, put something of aloe or myrrh reduced to juice, ointment, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and appearance of pus at the site of the basilic vein; put your hand over it, and if you feel the area soft to the pressure of your hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be sure not to place anything on the wound that we have described, for it might enter an artery; instead, apply a dry ointment to harden the area, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each according to its quantity of virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if it appears thick, let it flow until it becomes thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and outward, and needs bloodletting, that the wound be made larger, and the flames should be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and one must bleed little and often, and one should bleed by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and is better than bleeding from a long or wide cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body needs bleeding, one should give moist bread in pomegranate juice; if they are feverish, then three or four times before the bleeding. And if of a cold complexion, one should eat moist bread in rosewater syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger and cardamom, and perfumed syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he faints at the bleeding, after a large loss of blood, then he should drink a brothy soup and a subtle fragrant syrup, and use other things that we have discussed in the chapter on syncope, for the opening of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to open his arm and bleed again, when he is weakened by heavy bleeding, he should bleed a little at a time according to the amount of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to open their arm after the first bleeding, and they have a strong pulse, they should bleed at .7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to bleed elsewhere, one must bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is a great deal of blood in the body that has been heated and causes fever; therefore, you must draw out a large quantity, and widen the opening so that it drains out freely; then you should examine all the conditions of bleeding, and place your hand over his pulse as he bleeds, so that death does not come to the spot of the vein, which often happens when the surgeon is negligent; nor, when you see the arm loosening and the blood flowing a second time and the opening is closed, should you press firmly on it; nor, if it is bent, should you suddenly extend the arm, for that would be harmful; but let it be until he bleeds a second time; or you may touch it with the tip of the flame, so that the congealed blood in the vein melts and flows out, and then apply some warm water, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it until the abscess is relieved.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are healthy in terms of the vein in the head because it is composed of them.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bleeding is that the patient puts his hand in warm water until the vein turns red; then let it be bound lightly, so that the vein appears well, then bleed now through the middle, not the wide nor the long; and let the slit be wide, and let it be bled well near the joint of the hand, and if no blood comes out, put the hand in warm water again, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if it is winter, do not turn the hand back into warm water, because one puts it there more in winter than in summer; and the bleeding of this vein is safer than all other veins, because there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Bleeding the salvatele vein of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver; and here is the manner: stretch out the hand, and put it in warm water until the vein swells, as one sees; and if one bleeds it through the middle, and if you cut it all the way across, then it does no harm; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are completely stripped of flesh underneath, and then put the hand back in warm water if the blood congeals in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as necessary, put oil and silk on the vein to seal it quickly, and do the same for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the mouse, and do everything just as I told you about the right one.Et s’il aduenist que la main destre ou senestre sainie, et ne voit nule sang ne nule sainie, si met sus li piere et sus li membres oile de fong, si qu’ele se puet mouevra et eslonger; car ele est congelee.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The remedy for the disease of the sophene is good for all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the testes, and retention of fluid, and disease of the kidneys, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its remedy are that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs the vein until it pops, and ties something above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and up the foot there go many veins; therefore heal it at the widest vein, or at the ankle, whichever is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, then beware of the nerves that are underneath, and heal it across, as well as by copping; and let the flames be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and let the vein bleed well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the healer fails the first time, he should try again the second time higher up, because the site is salty; do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and thus do with the sophene of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The site of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its treatment extends to the pain in the hip, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the nature of his wound is such that the patient enters the bath, and twists his ankle three times, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then heal it in every way you can, and by crossing over; and it is better that you cover it, for the spot is safe, and it is very relaxed in many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not believe this, then heal a vein that opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and make it flow with blood as much as you can see, and then loosen the bandage, and place cotton on it and compress it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of cupping wounds
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leaches are made from horns, or iron, or glass; and bleeding is done in two ways: either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is done by burning is done in two ways: with fire, or without; and the cupping that is done by burning and bloodletting is done in 14 places on the body, of which one is at the very top of the head; and the other is in the neck; and two others are on either side of the neck; and the cupping is under the chin; and the cupping is on the shoulders; and the cupping is on the hips; and the cupping is on the arms; and the cupping is on the legs; and the cupping is on the ankles; and the cupping does not draw blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and because of this it does not weaken them at all, just as one does with vein-opening treatment; and it must not be administered with fire or without, in any disease that comes from fullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if, from necessity or habit, one must bleed, then we should do so at the beginning or end of the month, and at all times in between; for there are some who, when they need to bleed, feel heavy-headed; and some who experience congestion and redness on their face, head, and neck, and darkness before their eyes; and some who experience a flow of blood in their mouth, and swelling of the tongue, and bleeding gums; and there are those who faint, and see dark visions of pain, death, and other things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially if it is during the month, we command them to fast for three hours during the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps with headaches that originate in the eyes, and should not be done after the evacuation of the entire body; and this venting is in lieu of the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and should not be used by those of a cold complexion, or who have catarrh, as it does them great harm; and for these reasons, the elderly should not use it, nor those with cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are often healed by this, become oblate, and for this reason the leech should place the ventouse a little lower because of the risk of oblateness.Et si est en leu de la sainie del coeur, et que li home soit de chaude complexion, il est bon;
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation in the neck is located at the junction of the neck and the base of the skull, and this helps to relieve pressure on the feet, and to split the channel of the lung, and for belching and vomiting; and it should not be pushed too hard, as if held too tightly, it will cause discomfort or stomach and heart pain.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The second pair of ventilation holes in the neck help with headaches, and eye pain and inflammation, and with strangulation, and toothache, and are located at the junction of the skull; and you must instruct the surgeon to express his hand when placing it, so that he does not press the artery, and cause a gushing of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilation under the chin is good for diseases of the mouth and gums and similar diseases in the mouth; it is in the area of the veins on both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation of the armpits is good for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilation holes in the armpits are like three veins in the arm, as they draw blood from these large vessels; and command the surgeon not to push too deeply, as the area is bare of flesh, and beneath it lie nerves and arteries.Li ventosations des coutes est en leu de la sainie dou pis, et atrait sanc de li gros veine qui alent a li bras, et de la veine qui alent a la main; et si li dolors sont en la main, si covient que tu mettes tuit li poing sur le coud, et tu ventoses li cus del coud.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is placed on the back is good for hemorrhoids and illnesses below, and the cupping glass should be large and made of brass, because it needs to suck well; and sometimes if it breaks, it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping glasses on the legs heal very well, because they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains in the joints, and for pain in the hip, and the bladder, and they relieve swelling; and they are placed at the .ij. sophenes, and at the .ij. ankles, and yet they weaken the body after a long time, and bring fainting in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping glass is that you put it on first empty, and suck gently, and place it firmly, and move evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the skin reddened and swollen, and the blood appears; then let go, and reapply the cupping glasses, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are those who have such thick skin and clear pores: you should pierce only once, and make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, you should pierce twice: the first time to open up the pathway for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, you should pierce a third time; and when we want to draw a little blood, we only piercing once.Et se li sans est clers et legiers, si convient soulement ferir une fois, et traire legierement, et ne trop ne trop poc.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we bleed often; and if the blood is thick, we pierce it with a needle, and the ends [of the needles] should be heated so that the veins are pierced suddenly, and it suits those who have thick and tough skin and narrow pores that you grease the ends of the cupping glasses with aperitif and dissolutive oil: if it is in winter, with violet oil, or almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in summer, with watercress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is gross and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsam, or oil of anise, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person has soft skin and wide pores, no oil should be used on them, but they should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture, if they rise from ash, or myrrh water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large swellings should get up from old wine, or from dry water, or from a decoction of fennel or chamomile, or similar; and one should not bleed with a cupping glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one should not sleep after venesection, and it is necessary that he be warm when he is to be bled and when he has been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And be wary if the patient is choleric, and if the blood is too thin and inflamed; then he should take cold things like pomegranates and endives and lettuce with garlic, and similar; and eat little, and meat that is moist.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those of cold complexions should take syrup of honey, and moderate old and new perfumed wine, and drink little, and eat little, and small birds and pigeons; and on the day that one is bled, one must drink more than eat; and it is good to give some men a little triacle or musk before or after venesection, to fortify the principal members; and make the blood subtle, but those of hot complexions should not take it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.
