The cupping glasses that are applied without causing injury are those that are placed on the liver, and on the mumps, and on the gout, and on the belly, and the groin, and the armpit, because these limbs do not tolerate being injured on their joints, and it is only done to attract blood from one member to another, as we do when we apply cupping glasses to the breasts when a child is teething; to remove viscosity from a limb, as we do when we place cupping glasses on the belly and the groin to reduce the size of a limb; and it alleviates pain when there is congestion or a stone, and by its attractive power it may draw out the congestion or dislodge the stone; and it does the same when applied to the liver and mumps when there is retained wind, and these cupping glasses are administered empty merely to suck; and sometimes they are used with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this manner one fills the cupping glass with warm water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the fire cupping is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It is two inches wide and half an inch deep, and it has a small hole in the middle for threading a needle, made of bronze so as not to injure the patient when placed on the body; and there is a crossbar of bronze or iron inside, to hold a candle, and they are both large and small according to the illness and age of those who use them; for the ventouses used by children are different from those used by the elderly, and those used by the thin are different from those used by the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And you must place this ventouse on the body: take the candle of wax or the linen and put it inside the ventouse, through the crossbar, so that the flame is at the bottom of the ventouse and does not burn the patient; then place it on the body, and hold your fingers over the hole we mentioned, so that when you want to, the vapour will go out, and you remove the ventouse. Then take the linen as before, and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	Therefore, when using a cupping glass for the disease of pleurisy, for all acute illnesses, it has no stem or aperture, and is not removed until it is full of water, and is placed on the affected limb; and this is how it works:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are only removed when they are in water, and placed on limbs where cupping glasses cannot be used due to their size, such as the lips and gums, and similar places; and on bare skin, such as the finger or toe, and others like them; and the quality of their use is that when you find leeches that are in clear, still water without any movements, you should catch them; and put them in clean water until they become familiar with it and have nothing in their bellies; then they should be treated with bleeding and cupping, then rub the affected limb until it turns red, and place the leeches on top of it; and when they are full and start to move, if there is a suitable place for cupping, apply it, because it is very beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then raise the area with ash, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the bites heal too slowly after the body of the leeches, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place it over the bite until the bleeding is staunched; and if the bleeding increases, place ground vitriol or gall, or similar things on it, until it is staunched; or you can place half a handful of peeled peas over the area, and leave them there until they become warm to the touch, and it will then be staunched; and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches will not attach, then rub the area with fresh blood, or insert a needle so that the blood flows out, and then place them on it, and as soon as they smell the blood, they will attach; and when you see that they have finished feeding, then sprinkle powdered aloe and salt, or ash, over them, and they will let go.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is a remedy for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish people of this chapter have never seen any of the ancient books, nor have they read any letters; and for this reason, knowledge is strange in our land, for I have never found anyone good at it; and I know nothing about it except through the knowledge of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have acquired knowledge, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life. And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are introduced, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say in the prologue of this book the subjects of speech and the chapters where the wise man directs his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain occurs in someone, you should hurry to treat the patient from both sides, if nothing else holds him back, such as weakness of the body, or a fever, or old age; and if the weather is not very hot or too cold. Eat cold foods, that is, cold meats, and deer and goat meat, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you suspect a hot abscess or an eruption of material in the limb; then return the patient to his previous regimen.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, then one must feed the patient foods that promote swelling or have粘性, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and testes, and feet, and calf's stomach, and offal, and fresh fish, and full-bodied wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with much swelling the fracture will be reduced and heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And you should know that broken bones in the old and decrepit cannot be well set and joined according to their nature due to the dryness of the members, nor can those who are too tender, such as the bones of young children; but have no worry, reset the broken bone using the large tendons which stretch and join the member together, so that it enforces itself as it was before; and do not stop altogether in his work, and for this one should eat plenty of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you should know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from that of the foot, or of the leg; and I will tell you in this chapter about all types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another in piercing, like the point of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a complete fracture is a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And in each manner has its own remedy and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory comes to mind; and it is known that there is a fracture of the bone by the fact that the joint is twisted, and appears well through displacement, and sounds when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twist or crookedness in the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture; but it can still have a twist, or split, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you must not move it with your hand, but put on remedies that come later, and then now constrain it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And you should know that the fracture that goes in the armpit, and where the two parts are separated, they should now be put back together evenly, so that hot abscesses can come out; and if cold abscesses come out, then leave it for a day, until the abscess is soothed; then put it back to where you can easily and gently, and know that the restoration of the one is easier than the restoration of the one who has pieces; then strain it, as it should be done afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it is in two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or your hand if it is a small member, or at two cords, or at one cord and your hand; and put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, then bring them back together with all instruments in their places as you can, and be careful that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient; and join the two heads of the bones well according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand if it seems to you that it is not well-aligned: then dress it nicely, and do not stretch or press too much, as those who cause hot abscesses and contractions in the limb by their actions, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is ready, then carefully control the patient so that he does not move it, whether waking or sleeping, turning or in any other way; and be sure that the limb is so secured that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, then it is not yet ready, and you must put him in such a position that he feels no pain; and be careful that he is placed correctly so that no crookedness comes to him when he is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members vary in size, shape, and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs: these should be wrapped with soft linen; and for larger limbs, such as the thigh and leg, use a wide, tough ligature, for the wide ligatures embrace the entire large limb and constrict it equally from all sides, so that no swelling remains; then tie around it light bandages, 3 or 4 turns depending on the limb, and tighten your hand a little at every turn of the ligature, then go above the fracture and tighten less so that the fracture is slightly separated; then soften the ligature little by little, until you grasp most of the healthy area, then take another ligature, and wrap again over the broken area; then go to the part under the fracture and tighten gently, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we said in the first hour above; then place between the ligatures lint or bandages, so that they are all even, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put your splints well-fitted on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then apply something hot to soothe the abscess and reduce the swelling; leave it like this for several days. Then stretch out on a board, and let the arms be stretched out straight, the hands and feet turned upwards, and the body bent backwards; let them remain in this position for some time.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the board that one puts under the dislocation should be a little thicker and wider than the others; it should also be as long as is appropriate for the smallness or size of the limb. Then stretch out on the boards in the same way as before, then tie a bandage over the dislocation tightly but not too tightly, according to how loose or tight the ligature was before; it should be medium thickness, not too thick or thin, and made of soft linen. For if the bandages are thick, as I have seen foolish people do, making the ligatures out of twisted cords, this is a great error, for the ligature cannot be even if it is too thin, and there should also be less than a finger's width of space between each board.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore on the head from the stars after the binding, put beneath them linen or woolen bandages so that it does not hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the bones are broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not advisable to extend all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the member is large, you should not put splints on it for more than 5 or 7 days, or longer depending on your assessment of the hot abscess; and here is the method of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsion: take flour that is stored in the walls of the mill, cook it with plenty of egg, and apply this preparation, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common method of the plaster that restores fractures in various conditions, especially in women and small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for healing fractures and dislocations and twists: take 3 parts each of rosewood, ladanium, myrrh, and asafetida, and 2 parts each of gum arabic and mastic; 5 parts each of myrrh and aloe, 8 parts each of aloes and alechil; and grind them into powder, and mix them with egg white. If the person's complexion is warm, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it heals broken bones quickly, and is useful for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster that is good for torsion: take myrrh and balm of gilead, each 10 drams; frankincense and aloe, each 9 drams; acacia 6 drams; Armenian bole 10 drams, and grind well, and cook with water or plenty of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to make a plaster for joints and bones that have left their place, and to ease the resulting pain, and to treat the fracture: take new linen and soak it in lard and cooked oil, and apply it to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses and removing pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that heals broken bones: take dry fig leaves and dead nettle leaves, grind them together, and make plaster.Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. 3; mirre et aloes, ana .v. 3; alechil .viiij. 3; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastement, et vaut à plusieurs homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make a plaster for the restoration of a bone fracture, and to reduce swelling from an abscess:
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take marshmallow root, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, one part of each; and crush, and cook with wine, and if the member is scalded, cook it with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to make a stronger plaster than the previous ones, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of a member:
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of comfrey, and flax seed, borage, milk thistle, and marigold, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each one part; and grind, and cook with water of salt, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypocrites says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken member to restore it except for cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between soft and too hard.Et il dist ou livre que quant aposteme dure vinerent, qu’on doit prendre leveine de vezel, et la broier, et mettre sus l’aposteme, et porroier le membre; et si on le poinget a lor nassance, que li estraint les euelz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naisse.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen says that one should put on a broken member, to restore it, dry things that are a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe wood and incense, and similar things, as we have said.Et qu’on doit prendre le membra par la nassance et le tirer vers le haut et vers les costes en la circuite de la vaine; car il dit que si on tire le membre par la nassance, que li sang veult aler a sa place, ou il est necessere.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of ointment that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and human hair, or bird feathers, and beaver castoreum, and mix them together, and grind them, and make an ointment out of it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little after, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor does the bone move from its place; if not, loosen it by hand for several days. And if pain comes to the site, or itching, with rest or swelling, hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster immediately; and take light cloth, and sponge of sea moistened in water, and apply it to the site until the itching ceases, and the pain is soothed; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on lamb's wool, dampened in water or rose oil, and bind it with a bandage, so that you are sure of a hot abscess; and let the inflammation of the affected member subside, and the pain be removed, then begin the subtle binding again, and a little of the plaster, and do not tighten it as much as before; and subtly, until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is closed and red and painful and swollen all around, and you need ointment and bandages, then start again as you did first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If the limb does not show any signs of what we have described, then do not dislocate it until three, four, five or seven days; and sometimes you may leave it for twenty days, depending on what you observe, as long as the fracture remains open and the bone approaches the flesh; then restrain it more tightly than before, and increase the meat, as I have said earlier. If you see the site drying out more than necessary, know that swelling cannot occur there; therefore, wet it with warm water every time you dislocate it, and do this every third day, and loosen the ligature a little. Thus, swelling occurs in the limb through this method, and it quickly improves what the foolish people do, who restore the limb in a twisted manner: this is wickedness, and such actions are cowardly; I see nothing in them but weariness and doing it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of fractures, with varied appearances and distinct causes. Some fractures are caused by the impact of a sword, breaking the collarbone all the way to the shoulder socket, just like an ax or a pole; this type of fracture is called a "shoulder fracture.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts the bone without penetrating, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a concussion, or a splintering, or from the neck of a stone, or from falling on stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if the fracture is piercing, extending to the membrane below the bone, or on top of the bone, this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that is set in the bone as thin as a hair, and the crack is small, then this type of fracture is called  "capillary." And if the wound is caused by stone, or by falling, or by a similar object, and drives the bone fragment inward, and the site is hairy like the blacksmiths when they work on the furnaces; then the stone enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those with moist bones in the head, like the skull of a child; and it happens with all types of fractures where small fragments are displaced, just like tiles. I will speak about them in their respective places.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by their appearance, and by examination with the fingers, and by the corruption of the flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is discovered when one uncovers the bone and rubs it with a finger, then the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, take care with the symptoms of the disease; and if you see any bad signs, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, swelling, fever, eyes popping out and turning red, and other similar things in various conditions, then it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a surprising accident, and you hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the child comes to you first, and it is in winter, then you must cut the umbilical cord before the fourteenth day when you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, you must cut the cord before the seventh day, so that the thread under the cord does not rot and cause the accidents we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches just to the membrane that covers the brain, then you should split the fractured part thus: and it is necessary for you to grasp the head of the injured person, and remove everything on top of the bone in every way you can, and above the wound more gently than you can, and if blood flows when you expose the bone, or a pus-filled abscess, use the aid that is appropriate; and fill the area with soft rags moistened in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the pus-filled abscesses are soothed, and you are certain there will be no more bleeding; then begin to remove the bone all around, and this can be done according to two methods of operation: one method is that you cut straight down tightly in front, and the form is:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then make another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is to have various cuts, some narrow and some wide, and they should be pointed and made of iron; work gently so you do not cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard, you must pierce around it, so that you administer cuts with chisels, not so deep that they penetrate beyond the bone; and you should have a margin or circle on top, preventing the point from going beyond the bone; you should have several of these, so that each one comes in its place in the thickness of the bone, and you should have chisels for all tests; and this is the form of the three types of chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you place .i. probe on the bone and move your hand back and forth until you feel that the bone is pierced; then move the probe elsewhere a little later, and do this all around. Then cut into the space between the holes with an incision, and do this as skillfully and gently as you can, as we have said, until you draw out the bone with your hand or with one of the tools you have, like tweezers or pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinuses.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have penetrated and split the bone, it is necessary to remove the sharpness that remains from the bone with some instrument similar to an incisive instrument, but it must be more blunt and thinner than the other instruments; and if anything remains of the small bones or any scales, gently remove them with one of your instruments; then cure the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is that which Galen describes, which is much safer, and he highly recommends it, and his word is final.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover a part of the bone where the broken parts appear to be moving, and then, when you have uncovered this part, place underneath it the head of this lens-shaped instrument, for that is its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	Do not cut from one side only, for the part is swollen on both sides, so that the cutting will be towards the bone; then gently tap with a small mallet and gently strike the bone all around, being careful of the membrane underneath; if it adheres to the bone, gently loosen it, for it can be loosened without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone is not split all the way to the membrane and only cut slightly on top, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to return to that roughness, removing the scales with a very fine rasp so as to have various quantities to apply in each place according to what is most suitable, depending on the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you walk before great razors, and after smaller ones, and do not cease to do this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cuts and subtle breaks, you must administer treatment according to their nature; and this is something that is not answered by one who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the sinus is exposed, you should take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound and moisten it in rose oil and place it over the wound; then take another double cloth, soaked in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth, taking care to do this as gently as possible so as not to press on the sinus. Then apply a bandage above it without tightening it more than necessary to hold the wound; leave it for one or two days until the abscess is reduced, then loosen it and apply medicines such as roots of lilies, wheat flour, incense powder, aristologe, and similar substances; make a powder from these and place it on the wound, then apply other medicine that does not sting. Be sure that the wound is clean so that you do not leave any ointment in it or allow any pus to accumulate beneath the membrane of the brain, for when pus gathers beneath this membrane, it causes great harm.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no harmful accident occurs to the patient as we have said, for there is no doubt about it.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness does not come from the medicine that one has placed on it, because of its power, then you should take a portion of honey and three parts of rose oil and glue a cloth with it, and place it on the ulcer; then cure it in ways that are appropriate until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose are broken, or just one part, for there are two bones there; and below is cartilage, which does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should boil your little finger or a needle, and place it evenly in the break, inside your index finger, and bandage it tightly, so that the nail regrows according to its natural shape; do this gently and be careful not to cause the patient pain with your treatment.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the nose, and the bones cannot come together, then you should put it equal to the head of a rod that is somewhat thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, do this similarly, and try to restore it on the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then boil a tent of linen cloth at the tip of the nail where the break is.And if the break is in both parts, then do likewise, but hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, once the abscess has calmed down, then boil a tent of linen cloth at the tip of the nail where the break is.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you put on another one from the other side, if the fracture is there; and let the tents be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say one must moisten the tents with butter, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that is good, but one should wet the tent with egg white and flour; then leave it, as long as the bone is broken, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts in goose feathers instead of bandages, and then a soft cloth around, and holds the fracture, and blows the patient among; now do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if hot abscesses come in the face while you are working on it, put ointment or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in a poultice of daisy leaves.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no abscess comes out, then put on a plaster from the outside, of sesame flour and incense powder, cooked with egg white; then put on light pads, and do not bandage it tightly; and if the fracture is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with suitable instruments, then clean the wound, and stop the bleeding with things that constrict, and heal, as with plasters and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no wound within the nail, then treat it with tents, and put on splints until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated below, and there is no open wound, and the dislocation is only slight, and it is not broken in two, but rather displaced, one can tell easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is on the right side, to place your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the break is on the left jaw, then place your index finger of the right hand, and lightly plug the break inside, and release it with the other hand, and apply pressure evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is displaced on one side, then you must extend it one part, so that it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth, or cracking, then bind them with a thread of gold or silver or silk; then apply cerotum to the broken jaw, and place over it a double drape; and place over the drape a large, well-shaped splint, or a piece of leather the same size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it in place as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the jaw is changing shape, then loosen it on the third day, and then reset it to how it was changed; and apply plaster over it, made from mill powder with plenty of egg or flour of sisament, after you have removed the cerotum; and place over the plaster a light linen, and if the plasters stick, and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it takes to heal; many times it heals within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess comes, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine whether any piece of bone has been removed; then remove it carefully with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, dilate it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there is nothing left in it, then sew up the wound, if it is wide, and put over it some suitable poultices to promote healing.
de la forcele	of the fire
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The collarbone breaks in several ways in front of the shoulder, and the break occurs in three different ways: it can be broken and separated into two pieces, which is the easiest to heal; or there can be a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the treatment is when there is no wound with the break, you must have two assistants: one holds the shoulder where the collarbone is broken, and the other stretches the neck towards the affected side; then use your fingers to align the broken bone so that it is set correctly, with no visible displacement or misalignment.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you need more leverage, place a round piece of cloth or linen under the shoulder, as thick as necessary; then lift and gently pull on the collarbone, holding the patient's shoulder steady with your hand, and align the broken bone as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder out of its socket because it comes up easily, then the patient should lie on his back, and place one ear down under the shoulder, and the assistant pulls the shoulder downward, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then press the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it broken, then you must cut over it; and gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot join because of any swelling, then apply the cautery to one of the cuts that you have made in order to draw out the pus.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it should resemble a spoon, and not be curved, and be as wide as is appropriate according to the size of the bone and the extent of the work; and it should have two prongs, as you can see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, depending on the nature of the wound that you created when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut open the wound, and if the route is small, or if you doubt there is a hot abscess, then pack the wound with linen and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a deep abscess comes, moisten a cloth in rose oil and ass's milk and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The stretching of the bone, when there is no wound or fracture, is to place upon the bone the plaster made from mill dust and egg white, and put light sponges on top, and if necessary, place a spear underneath the splint; then take a very large band, about the width of a palm, and place two layers of linen over the sponges and plaster; then take a thin rod, three digits wide and long, and wrap it around the band so that the end of the band hangs down; place the rod upon the fracture, and wrap the band around the neck, and under the healthy shoulder, and under the injured shoulder; then adjust each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture in place, and you clearly see that the rod does not move over the broken bone, reward it every day, and when the ligature becomes loose, tighten it; have the patient lie on his back, and when he sleeps, place a small pillow under the shoulder to raise the joint; thus, the force of the dislocation will lessen through the raising of the joint, or tie the arm to the neck for up to twenty-eight days; then start the plaster again if you see that it is needed, and adjust and leave it, until it is healed; and it is usually healed within twenty-eight days, but some people take less time.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It sometimes happens that the shoulder is broken or dislocated in a large or small way, and one does not feel it except by touch; then one applies the bandage according to the shape of the fracture, and repositions it according to its natural form, in every way one can; then one puts powder from the mill with plenty of egg white on the site, and light padding, and lays a double cloth over it; then one places a broad and thin splint, a little broader than the shoulder, and if underneath the splint there is swelling anywhere on the shoulder, then one applies that swelling with padding made of linen, so that the splint lies evenly; and then one binds it very tightly all around with a large bandage, so that the splint does not move from its place, and one checks the binding every day; and every time it loosens, one tightens it again, and puts the splint back in place if it has moved, and lets the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder is restored within 20 or 25 days. And when this number of days is completed, one releases the binding, and be sure, for it is not a bone that sets easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone pokes out in front, and not underneath the heart, they cut above it, and the bone, and do as we said in the breaking of the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The penis is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; it often breaks at the tip.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it inclines downward, and the patient experiences great pain and difficulty urinating and defecating, and sometimes vomits blood, and the hair grows from the broken bone, and he feels great harm.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that the patient lies on his back, and places a cushion between his shoulders, then presses his shoulders, and brings together the two ribs with his hands, and skillfully adjusts the positioning so that the bone is set correctly; then he applies plasters and bandages over the fracture site with a thin layer of salt, or other lightweight material, and wraps it in a cloth, and ties it to the broken bone, ensuring it doesn't move; and he winds the bandage around the body, and tightens it comfortably, and checks every hour, and if it softens, he tightens it; and if it needs to be loosened due to corrosion or itching at the site, or pain or an abscess, he should hurry and loosen it, and clean away any discharge that has accumulated, and reapply the treatment; then he reapplies the plaster, and tightens it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of ribs only occurs in the thick ones near the back, and at the top inside, and they only bend because they are slippery; and one feels it well upon examination with both hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is to reset the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the ointment and compress it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of ribs is declining inward, then the patient feels great pain, and stabbing, as well as pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; and also has pains in his sides, and is short of breath and vomits a large amount of blood, and it is a serious illness, and the ancients held it in high regard.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, in order to push out the fracture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make an incision for a hot abscess unless one has already formed.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if there is one, then drain it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one should place cups on the site to draw out the inflammation, and this is reasonable; however, there is a risk that the cupping will draw out the vital spirits due to weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the place with soft woolen cloth in hot oil, and put a tent between the ribs to make the space around it even, then it is cured with a poultice of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient experiences great pain where the bone is poking through the skin, and there is doubt about the condition, then one must split the skin above the broken rib, and place an instrument beneath to ward off the hernia; then one must cut the bone, and gently pull, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat with ointments until healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if heated blisters arise, put wet cloths in rose oil and apply to the area; and treat the site as needed for the blister, and let him lie quietly on his side where he should be, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture in his neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a break in the bones of the neck, and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will recover or not, take note if his hands are soft and swollen and dead-looking, and he cannot move or straighten them, and when you prick him with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that in many cases it is deadly, and if he can move and feel pain when the joints are extended and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the ailment will be cured if treated properly.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar condition arises in the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will recover or not, take note if his feet are swollen, and if the symptoms are in his hands, and there is windiness and urination without control; and when he lies on his stomach, there is urination without control.Quant il y a egestion sens volonteit sus lou ventre et em dos egestion et ventositeit, si ne deust on leu demourer mais se tu le remets a leu, si ne pot demourer; et quant il est sur leu, si saut egestion sens volonteit.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is sleeping on his back and wants to turn over, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	You should know that it is deadly; therefore do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these symptoms do not occur, then the condition is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you apply an ointment to the spine if there is a hot abscess, using rose oil or the yolk of a hard-boiled egg, until it is soothed; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and they must not sleep on the side where they feel pain, until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, one must cover the wound over the heart; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a single stitch, then treat the wound with ointment, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow", place your thumb of your left hand into your pouch, and hold it equal to the other hand in your power, then apply the plaster and the bandage on top, if you need to; then tighten it, and if there is a dislocated bone, do the same, remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	from the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It sometimes happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does, there will be a slight diminution in size at the head; and they become long and decline towards the buttocks, and cause pain in the affected area, as well as swelling and bruising.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is to extend your hand over the fracture; and know which is the broken part and its shape; and if the break is only at the head, then put the broken part in its natural position.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it inclines inwards, then let the patient lie on his belly so that the restoration of that fracture may be prepared for.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then put on the plaster, then put on a board of wood or horn, and tighten the fracture so that it does not move; and apply the place under the ribs until the fracture is healed.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if painful abscesses come, do not touch them until the painful abscesses are soothed, and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and tighten it as it should be, unless there is some bad incident; and that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoires is that which is between the neck and the head of the shoulder; and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two methods: one is that you take a rod of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends with a cord, and hold them upright, and put the patient on a seat; then let him lay his broken arm on the rod, so that it comes to rest, and have a curve of the rod, then lean over something heavy or let the minister stretch it downward; then have the patient apply pressure on the break with both hands together, so that the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one holds the patient upright, and ties his hand to his neck, then command two ministers, so that one pulls what is above the break with their hands, and the other pulls beneath by one of the cords, and each stretches his part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, then constrict the ligament below the fracture, and above it, and extend each of the ministers to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.
