And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, then you should put one bandage in the middle of the shoulder and the other towards the neck, below the fracture; and likewise, if the fracture is towards the neck, then the bandages should be applied lightly without labor, so that the fracture remains even both on the shoulder and on the neck; then make the fracture even as it should be, and constrict it, unless warm abscesses come about.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if hot abscesses come to it, then do not press until 7 days, and put soft linen in vinegar and rose oil on the hot abscesses until they are soothed; then press it, and the way to press is that you put the ointment on the fracture, then assemble the arm above the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the bandage, and press above the shoulder, and above the arm, so that the arm is in place of stars, if no thing moves it, or the bone is moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone moves, then use stars, and put a larger and stronger star on the fracture than the others, and let there be between each star 2 inches of space, and let each star be as large that it passes the fracture by 3 inches on each side; then press upon the stars, thus as I said at the beginning of the chapter, above the fracture, more forcefully and less in moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the stars, and the constriction, as we have said, at the time that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the hot abscess, let it be bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine the bandage every three days, so that itching or swelling does not come to the site, or the pus cannot come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	As we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, do not unbind it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and place beneath the shoulder a pillow filled with wool, equally soft, and examine every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken member does not move, or the bandage become softer; then it will heal through the power of medicine, and give him the food we mentioned earlier, in such a way that the food is very subtle at first; and when he begins to recover, let the food become thicker.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be wrapped for forty days altogether; and then one must loosen it and administer baths and ointment medications to direct the place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is bad and swollen, it remains wrapped for 50 days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the broken arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the 'bony', of which one is small, and it is the one that follows the armpit; and the other is large, and it is the one that is underneath, towards the little finger; by chance, only the large bony bone may break, or the small one, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, their restoration and healing are easy; but when the large bones are broken, their healing is more difficult and painful than when they are broken all at once.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is broken, it should be extended slightly and set evenly.Et quant li grans fosciles sont brisiez, si convient que li membres est remuiez, et li foscile le plus grant qui a l’estremeite soulevier.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And when the larger bones are broken, the limb should be moved and the largest bone which has the extremity raised up. And if it is the larger bone, then it should be stretched more strongly; he should lie on his back, with his pouch of the hand higher than the rest, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and have the affected side crossed over him, and a pillow in front of him higher up so that the patient does not undergo any labor; then extend the minister's arm at the part below to his hand, or to the wrist, and another minister above it.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he puts the mirror in front of him, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break there are pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is any dislocation that grabs the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as we have said before, on the bone and the artery.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it singularly in this chapter; take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration boils appear, then apply a poultice made from cerate of rose oil and white wax, so that it is neither too hard nor too soft; and bind the poultice gently on top, until the boils are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerate, and apply the plaster made from mill-powder with egg white, then put on the splints, and let the splint on the fracture be a little stronger and a little larger than the others; and know that he must have six splints on the arm in various positions: let the fracture be in one of the bones, or in two; and press harder on the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as they heal, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages on top of the fracture be soft and moist, not hard or rough; and let the thread used to tie them be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And examine the limb and the joint after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, you should wash the limb with warm water until the itch is relieved; and let the limb not be pressed or restrained from resting.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then restart the stretching, and if the joints are softened and the bones separated, address it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if one is wary that the nourishment cannot reach the member because it is too tight, then one must loosen it a little and leave it thus for some days, until the nourishment flows, and then tighten it again.Et se li os se desevrent, si covient qu’il soit estrais adés fors; et li norrissemens ne peut venir au membre por ceu qu’il est trop estrois.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have described happen to the patient, then do not release him until 20 days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or, if nothing else happens to the patient, then he can wash his hands and neck, and let his neck be even, and guard against movement and exertion, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is healed in 30 or 35 days, and perhaps in 20 days, depending on the mixture and the complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and around the fingers there are few fractures, and only swelling comes from it many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or swollen, the patient should sit upright, and extend his arm in front of him, keeping his elbow bent at a right angle; then he should place his hand on a flat surface, and the practitioner should straighten the broken bones and bring them into alignment; then they should apply the poultice and bandages if there are no abscesses, and then put on a splint according to the size of the injury; finally, they should wrap it in a single linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the peritoneum around the navel, make a sponge out of cloth, and instruct the patient to hold it to his broken navel; then hold it with a long piece of cloth, and the stamp should be as large as the palm of your hand, and you must hold it firm, as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the forearm, you must place a stamp on top and another one underneath the wrist so that the hand is open and straight; then tie it all around the arm and stop the bleeding between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture is in one of the fingers, if it's the thumb, set it straight as it should be, and hold it with the palm; and if you see fit, place a small straight stamp to raise the fracture, and don't move it; and if the fracture is in any other finger like the index or others, set it straight and tie it with the adjacent healthy finger; either tie them all together while holding them steady, or place a stamp on top as you would on the thumb; take care in the healing process and in the application of a hot abscess, and treat any wound that arises, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and one can see this when it turns front and back; its restoration is to bind one ligature above the break and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extends each bandage to its part equally; and this is when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, then one of the ligatures should be towards the armpit, and the other ligatures below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, then the ligature should be on the opposite side of the knee, and the extension should be downwards; then the surgeon should put the bone back into its natural alignment with his two hands, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, unless an abscess forms there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm down and then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is done in this way.The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap a long, folded bandage around the fracture two or three times, and leave any excess, then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and tie a long string between the thigh and the leg on the opposite side of the knee, and have the ends of the string come up from above; then go back over the leg and the thigh with the bandage, then place splints on top of the fracture, and put one splint on top of the bone in the leg; then tighten the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to adjust the tension, then start tying the two heads of string that you have tied between the leg and the thigh three or four times over the fracture; and the more you go up above the fracture, the less you should tighten it; then feel the two heads of string that you have tied, and tie three splints that are on top, then return to the bottom at the foot end of the string, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, so that no abscess or swelling or other sign develops.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If an abscess develops, untie the bandage and address what has formed, as we have said many times before. If there are pieces of bone protruding, they should be removed if possible; if not, then the area should be slit open and drained, then treated as described until the wound is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Sometimes the thigh or arm may be broken in this way when splints are used, as in the case of a dislocation; nonetheless, the treatment described will not harm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And you shall know that the thigh is restored in one day or a little less or more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the back of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the kneecap there is little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a perforation; and it happens in every wound, whether with pain or without, and everyone feels it.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to put equal pressure on what is torn at his fingers, as long as it can be; then put the ointment, and if necessary put a round splint, and bind it as it should be, then observe all the dispositions that we have mentioned in other fractures, such as hot abscess and similar; then put to each accident what it needs, as long as it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break in the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called the "mustelz" and the other the "foscile". The breaking of these bones is treated the same as that of the arm, and the operations are the same in both cases. And if both bones are broken at the same time, the leg turns completely backwards.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the subtle bone is broken, then it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it can be seen clearly, and it turns inside out.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, use extension, and set it straight, and tie the splints evenly; but if the fracture is ugly, and there are several pieces, then the extension should be lighter and easier; adjust it according to your skill.Et s’il est brisie de la partie du bas, et ne peut demourer a son leu, si convint que li ramonnes la dislocation premierement, et il i a grant dolor.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, then take two strips of wood that span the leg from one side to the other, and are as long as the leg from the knee to below; then wrap two bands around them above and below, and tie it in the middle, and at this time the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and so is well; and some administer a splint as long as the leg, and it is made of wood, and they put the leg into it to prevent movement, and properly apply it to the break where there is pain; and move the leg every day to see if there is any hot abscess or other accident; and treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the break of the bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no break, but at times a break occurs in the bones of the foot and also in the two small bones, and there is only bruising with various dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If it happens to the leg bones that they are broken and you see the bones on top of each other, then put the patient's foot down on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, and then put your foot on top of his, where the bones are raised, then press them until they return to their place; then apply the ointment and poultice on top, and under the leg in the abdomen, a small piece of wood with two smooth sides, then bind it to the leg, then wrap bandages around, and other things you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three or four days have passed, loosen the binding, for you will find the bones even if they are broken or displaced.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if one or more of the fingers are broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then put on the broken finger a splint according to the length of the finger, and let it be a little wider, then put under the foot that small piece of wood I mentioned before, and bind it tightly; and if there are one or two or more broken, put on each finger a splint according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the wood tightly under the foot; and let the top of the wood press firmly against the abdomen of the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other breaks, from what we have already said; and treat each case as it should be treated.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of a woman's pelvis are broken, make her sit up straight, then lean forward to the small of the back, and hold her from behind. Then fill the vagina with cotton wool, and place a finger inside; then stand the woman up, and gently rock her back and forth, and the cotton will pop out as it reaches the opening of the pelvis, and the bones will return to their correct position with the finger. And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished, insert it again, and do this for seven days; the break will be healed. Then take a bladder from a lamb, and tie a tube to the opening, and blow into the tube until the bladder is inflated inside: the pelvis will return to its correct position. Then fill it with cotton wool, and leave it for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the shoulder of man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the case of the hip-bone; and these fractures are not hidden from him who devotes attention to his art and studies my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fractures indicate in many ways the right way to restore them; understand this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	For a broken penis, take a goose's gullet and insert the penis into it; then wrap it tightly with cloth and leave it for three days, checking on it every day, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as in the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be bled immediately, so that the bleeding we have described can attest to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound bleeds, then apply Vitriol, if you have nothing else, and then restart the healing of the fracture in that same hour or that day, if no abscesses come from it.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come from it, then leave off the healing until the next day, until the abscesses are settled, and do not touch them on the third or fourth day, for you would bring about a bad accident by doing so.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the uncovered chest, you should gently put it in place with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not apparent to you so that you can put it in place with your hands, then use this instrument of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and for this, it is necessary for the surgeon to press down on it three or four times, depending on each case of a broken bone; and let it be round and slightly thick, so that it does not bend during compression on the affected limb, and let it be sharp in front, and thicker from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called «palainche», because the curved head of the bone should be placed upon the prominent end of the other bone; and it is put in once, so that it may come back, and be even with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot well seize the bone, then you must shave the head of the bone, so that the instrument may have hold of it.Et se li os sont troves et la chair adessuz, si convint que tu le traies a la corde, tant ke la chair soit sus l’os; car ancil la corde ne poait apeler li os, et non li os apeler la corde.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then cut into it with an appropriate instrument, either a chisel or a knife, to your ability; and then pull out what remains in the bone of splinters and tiny shards.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is moved back into place and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Then make sure it is in its proper place, moisten the cloth with black wine, and cleanse the wound if it has become soiled; do not apply ointment or anything else to the wound that would cause pus and corruption to form; then apply a poultice after you have reset the bone, leave the wound exposed, and cover the surrounding area according to the size of the wound, being careful not to restrict the wound with the bandage. This is what foolish people often do, causing death or corrosion on the patient at times; and the pressure should be softer on this type of fracture than on others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is deep or large, and you fear an adverse event as we have said, and you feel pain in the area, then do not apply a poultice; but wrap around the wound, instead of a poultice, hard pieces of cloth, and tie them tightly.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days a swelling on the wound, then remove what you have put over it completely, and apply an ointment that heals wounds, such as an ointment of four-fold remedy and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you should loosen the bandage on the limb twice a day, in the morning and at dusk, until it is healed and closed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And one must prepare the limbs in such a way that the bowstring runs smoothly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they persist for many days, and it cannot heal but keeps dislocating the bowstring, know that there are small pieces of bone causing this, so you must probe the wound with a hook and remove all these displaced pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula or any other kind of corruption appears, you should treat it according to what he says in the chapter earlier.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when a bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the thigh or shoulder bone, and similar large bones, do not treat it at all, for many die from it, but leave it to heal over; perhaps it will fall out after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	And when a bone is broken on the limb, and the limbs are dislocated, you must reset it to its place and hold it as long as you can; and if it will not stay in place, then you must reset it, but it is not good for it to be too long dislocated.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Many times after the healing of a fracture, especially when it is near a joint, an unsightly appearance results in the limb; and by chance, the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take heed therefore if the patient becomes constipated: use astringent medicines like aloe, incense, myrrh, and sarcocolla, mixed with wine, egg white, or garlic; place them on the wound as poultices and bind them tightly, leaving them in place for several days; then remove the bandage and repeat this treatment until the swelling is reduced. You may also apply a plaster made from finely ground stone to draw out the inflammation. If the injury has turned into a hard lump like stone, and it needs to be removed, cut away the superficial tissue and excise the excess growth. Alternatively, you may refer the patient to a surgeon who can remove it, healing the wound afterward.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weakened after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed, but the limb remains weak and delicate, this can occur due to several reasons: one reason is that it was bound too tightly and not properly; another is that there were too many ligatures, preventing nourishment from reaching the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or from too much movement, especially before its time; or because there is a lack of blood in the body, resulting in weakness.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you should make the patient eat, and make the body tender, so that the blood is multiplied within him; and administer to him baths, and give him joy and leisure; then apply pitch to the limb, so that the pitch attracts the great swelling, and frequently moisten it with warm water, until the swelling goes down into the limb; and restore it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	then the limb will become straight again after recovery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after recovery and the broken bone is exposed, and the shape of the limb is deformed, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function; so do not believe the foolish who say that one must break the limb again completely, and many fools have done this in our land; and these actions are blamed, and great harm may come from them, and even death; all the same, if the dislocations and wounds are fresh, then one should apply warm water or herbs which soften, such as leaves of plantain, and roots, and mallows, and similar medicines that soften the swelling; and make an emollient ointment, such as thyme well prepared, and you take the mucilage of plantain, and cook it with suet or sisam oil, and apply an ointment to it; or you take figs, fat them with hog's dung, and grind similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the joint is dislocated by constantly rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let the limb be moved every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the crookedness is woke and hardened like stone, and needs to be cut out with iron, then it must be covered up to the bone, with a sharp incision made lightly; and put bandages and study into the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to someone, one must now bring it back without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the place will swell and sometimes it is reset in its place; therefore one should not move it at the hour when it is swollen: many times it causes inflammation and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient be bled, then left alone until the abscesses are soothed; then bathe the limb with hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and cure each member as the cure will come to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Then the jaws become dislocated, and the dislocations of both are according to two manners: either they are a little pushed out of their places, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the bottom, and saliva flows from the mouth which he cannot hold in, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue is enveloped in speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through several dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you should reset it quickly without tarrying; and let the assistant grip the head of the patient, and plug his ears with his fingers from one hand in the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if there are two parts of dislocation; and let the other fingers be straight, to make them equal; and instruct the patient to soften their jaws and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And she looks at the mirror, as long as it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the jaw is dislocated, especially if both jaws are together, then they should be treated with hot water and oil, as long as they are gently reset; do not pull hard to reset it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back into alignment and the mouth of the dislocation is closed well without softening, then put it on moistened cloths in cerate made of rose oil and wax, then tie it lightly with soft ligatures; and let the patient sleep on his back, and keep his head steady between two pillows so that he does not move to the right or left, nor strain to yawn, but take light food until the pains are relieved and the jaw is healed; then let him eat what he likes lightly, and do not exert himself to open his mouth to eat and drink until the jaw is well sealed and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be returned to their place in an hour, and are not converted to their own place, then fevers and accustomed sods come, and by chance a solution of the belly, and by chance vomiting pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then you know that it is destruction; and many times the person to whom it happens dies within eight days.If the mandibles are not reduced in time, death will follow, as we have seen happen many times.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceless one cannot dislodge it from the ribcage within its path and from the foot, and it is dislodged sometimes by force, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then press the area firmly with your palm, and it will return to place; then put on the ointment and bandage, and tie it tightly; and the shoulder which is towards the neck cannot dislocate; if it does, and it dislocates at any time, then reset it to its place as we have said; then put on the ointment and bandage, and tie it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the same way the shoulder of the spleen is reset when it has been dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one, it dislocates at the part of the axilla below; the second is at the part of the foot; and sometimes it dislocates above, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves; and often it dislocates below towards the axilla, especially in those who have little flesh, for in them it pops out suddenly; but in those who have enough flesh, it pops out slowly and goes back in slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that they have a concussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you must test it to make sure, and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And you will know the dislocation when it is below towards the axilla, and there will be a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a manifest diversity between them; and you will find a pit at the top of the shoulder, and under the axilla at the top of the shoulder, just as if it were an eye; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way; and also, if it is dislocated above, it is not hidden, for you will see it clearly at the top; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to fix when it is new, or when the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is for the assistant to lift the affected hand up, then place their fingers under the shoulder, and forcefully lift the joint upwards in its place; and the assistant lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then places it back down; this should be done quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If it does not return within a few days as we have said, then the patient should be bathed in warm water and given soothing and softening poultices, such as decoctions of alder, fenugreek, and milkweed in water; then the patient should lie on their back, with a layer of equal wool beneath them, neither too soft nor too hard, and place their heel on the wool, and lift the shoulder blade gently, and draw the hand of the affected side; while another assistant holds the head of the patient so that it does not move downward; this shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that it is dislocated again, do it according to this manner: have a man who is larger than the patient stand present; he should be straight toward the hip, push the shoulder blade underneath the affected side, and lift the armpit so that the patient hangs from the arm; then another assistant draws the hand of the affected side downward toward the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the disease is too slight, then one can put upon him some heavy thing, and the dislocation will return at once.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is reset in another way also: one takes a long wooden peg which is as thick as the palm of the hand and neither too big nor too small; this is placed beneath the patient but covered with a thin cloth, and the patient should stand upright while this is done; then his hand is extended downward on the other side and the joint will return to its place at once; and if it does not return despite all these things we have said, then do this cure: take a peg two arms long and four fingers wide which has a pointed end so that it may enter deeply beneath the shoulder according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie a soft cloth to the tip of the brand so that the brand does not strike the patient; then place it under the shoulder joint of the patient, and extend his arm above the shoulder, and tie the shoulder to the brand, and the arm at the hand, then place the arm on a wooden board, and extend the hand downward, and let the body hang on the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, however it may be, you must then place a woolen ball under the joint, then apply the prepared plaster of flour from the mill, with incense and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around, then tighten it under the joint gently, and tie the string over the plaster, and embrace the hand to his chest, and let the hand remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eat little, until the limbs are healed, for he will heal faster; and then eat more after five or seven days, and move him; and if he is stiff and not柔軟, then he is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has come out of its place because of moisture or for any other reason, then you must administer cauteries to it in three places, as is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot lift his arm upstream, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations which are towards the bottom, and in the breasts, or behind, are made by pushing and stretching with the hands, and one administers it elsewhere; and heal until it is healed.Et si li nerf ne puet estre en son leu, adonc covient qu’il fie estrit a la coine, et li membrez remuez, et li nerf estenduz; et si il n’est pas sanez, adonc covient que tu le vives, et le menes en li lieures; et si il ne puet estre en son leu, si covient qu’il fie estrit a la coine, et le membrez remuez.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing there is cramping in the limb, and later with movement, then the patient should be bled many times until that cramping is relieved and returns to its former nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder joint
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	You should know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated by pins, and it returns by pins; and if it is dislocated from all sides, and especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not reduced, for one can see and feel it well; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick neck with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is broken, and he cannot bend his arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it as soon as the abscess has broken, for if the abscess breaks, it will be painful to reset; and by chance it may not be able to be reset at all, especially when it is in the back; then it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and by chance death may come.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be reset, that you extend his hand with your two hands; and let his arms be spread out, and his hands from the wrist according to the elbow, around and underneath, and push the joint into its socket at the base of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in the front, it will return when he bends his hand towards his palm, and puts pressure on the wrist which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not want to return to his place, then he gives strong extension; and there are two ministers who extend the arm, and they hold it so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side; and when you have wrapped a long, wide cloth around it, and the minister has joined the joint with his hand, then anoint the joint with some oil to soften the joint, then press the joint firmly until it returns; and when it is in place, apply a dry plaster with egg white, and stretch it firmly, and bind the arm to the neck of the sick man, and leave it for a few days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not setting well, repeat the plaster and the bandage, and leave it for a few days until it is set firmly; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the joint is moved back into place and it becomes immobile, then bathe and rub it gently, and press until the pain subsides. Or, place a fat sheep's pad over the joint, leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and have him enter the bath; and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the pad back on, and then enter the bath again; do this two or three times until he is healed. If you see fit, place warm cow manure with butter on top, and hold it in place; then it will return to its natural state.
li dislocation de la main	dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is healed, and the return is lighter than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place gently, in the same hour that it was dislocated, so that the joint is swollen or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	The procedure for moving the joint back into place is to have the patient lay his affected hand on a table, and extend his fingers; then you look at it and move it until it is in line with the joint, as if he were placing his palm over the joint itself, and you adjust it until it is aligned. Then you must check that it is in the right position; next, have him place the back of his hand on a table while you extend and flex his fingers.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient lie his hand on a table, and the surgeon place his hand over that part where the joint appears.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it now goes back into place, that is good; if not, then strain it with soothing poultices on the affected area, and leave it thus without trying to move it again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it and you cannot put it back in place after several attempts, then let the joint remain out of position; and do no harm to the patient until his hand is strong again and he can grip things once more. Then you will know that either the nerves or the arteries are cut; there is nothing else to be done but to strain it with fire, close to the affected area.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, apply the plaster that we have described, then hold it and leave it for five days, then loosen it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any swelling, then soak it in warm water and rub it until it is healed.Et s’il a aucune estresse par la main, si le moille d’aigue fraiche et le frote, et met sus l’emplaustre que nous avons dit; car il ne doit pas demourer longuement en tel estresse, mais estre remu en aigue fraiche, car il n’est pas bon qu’il soit longuement en telle estresse.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers are dislocated on one side or the other, sometimes at the back of the palm or at the base of the hand; then you must draw the finger towards the affected area and hold it there; leave it for two days, and then put it in line with the rest of the hand that day. Do not let him use his hand for anything, as we have said, but just move it; do this often until it is healed. Do the same if it is dislocated at the base of the hand, and do as described above until it is healed.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	the dislocation of the spine in the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine in the back or neck is dislocated, there is no treatment, for death comes quickly.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the evacuations occur without voluntary effort, and one cannot hold them back; and often a limb is paralyzed, in either the two legs or the two arms or one; and often the skin turns black in four places: that which turns black at the back is called 'paralysis': the cure is that you must find out whether the paralysis came on from childhood; if so, there is no cure for it nor any hope of recovery.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient authorities describe at great length, but I have abridged it according to my understanding and have devised instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in paralysis which comes to the foot in front, there is no cure nor health; and also that which comes directly to both sides, and one cannot cure it except by the one which comes directly at the back, as I said; and it must be that the patient lies flat on his face in one place, and has a support under him so that he does not bend; then insert the cautery iron into the ground at the head, and another at the feet, and tie a string under the seat of the paralysis, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two attendants hold the strings, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two cautery irons; and they must be tied tightly, the cautery iron as we have said, and the attendant puts his palms on the spine until it comes back.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a table three yards long, and lie under the wall, and let the patient be on their side, and put the head of the table under the wall, then place the middle of the table on the spine; and let the patient put their feet on the other end of the table, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see it, do it again in the turn that turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should put two torches at the head of the patient's arm, and two others by their feet, and there should be between each torch, above and below, a palm of space in length; and there should be in each torch a hole, where the thread turns, and the torches are firmly in the ground so that they do not move; and between each two torches there is a turning torch, on which the threads turn, and there are two small torches at the turns, each a palm in length, for turning the thread; and then tie the thread that is among the pegs to the thread toward the head, and the other thread toward the feet to the other thread, and each of the ministers turns their thread to all the thread, and the master places the spine evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, then put on a desiccant plaster with an egg yolk, and then the poultices, and then the cushion of a pillow three fingers thick, which colors the area of the swelling and the healthy part of the spine; then tie it with a bandage as we said before, and use the patient's subtle cooling medicine until he is healed. And if anything comes at the end of healing, one should administer softening and soothing medicines with the cushion we mentioned earlier. Sometimes they give them a piece of plywood, and sometimes the appearance comes in the back on the spine, and people think it is dislocation; but it is the bone that protrudes, so one must not presume to touch it, for it could bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the shoulder only come from dislocations, and not as with other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and most inside, and slightly dislocated in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is such that when one joins the affected leg with the healthy one, the affected one is longer, and the affected knee joint appears more than the healthy one, and the affected one cannot bend his knee towards the fire; and the part that is nearby is swollen with a hot abscess because the head of the thigh bone has come there.
