Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes as a defence, is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who it happens to in front, are that his leg is well according to its accomplishment; nevertheless, he does not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot go before, and he retains his urine, and the veins swell, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who it happens behind, are that he cannot bend or straighten his knee, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the veins are softened, and the head of the thigh is at the place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this kind of dislocation are that you examine whether the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its condition, then there is no cure for it; and it must not be allowed to become stiff.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for that which is the fresh dislocation, and it is of the four kinds of dislocation, you hurry to return the joint to its place, and stretch it both inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and does not need any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, you must prepare a strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or with a cord tied above the knee; and another minister stretches his hand over in such a way that he pushes his hands under his heels, then he is bound with a strong cord over the thigh; and another holds his head with a cord; and they stretch upward and downward all at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once and remains pendant.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of stretching is common in four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, you must apply a bandage to his appearance. When the dislocation is in the buttocks, you must lie the patient on his healthy side, then place the bandage over the root of the thigh, and the part under the hip, then stretch the bandage upward toward the hip and the armpit; then another minister grabs his arms and embraces the large part of the patient's thigh, and stretches it forcefully outward: it will return to its place now; and this type of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you cannot reduce the dislocation in the manner we have described, then you should bind both feet of the patient together with a strong suede thong around the heels and knees; the affected leg should be extended two handbreadths further than the other. Then let him be suspended from a pole, with his arms hanging down two cubits from the ground. Then command one assistant to grasp the head of the thigh firmly, and another assistant, hanging alongside the patient, to grasp the thigh forcefully, for the joint will now return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is reduced, let the patient lie as we have said in that which concerns gout, and tighten the thong around the leg and foot; then put two torches, one at the head and one at the feet, and place the torch between the thighs of the patient in the region of the groin; and have moist bandages laid on, so that he does not scorch himself, then extend each assistant away from him, and the surgeon should apply pressure evenly over the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns to place, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, then place him on a table and press it as we said before in the section on dislocations, and lay the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the sick leg gently, and according to what I have said; and put the one looking at it on top of the sore shoulder, then press with the other hand, and they lean down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is outward, then one must not extend the patient downward, nor lift him up from the ground, but he should be as if his hip were dislocated outward, as we said about lying on both hips; and he should lie on his face, with the bandage stretched as we said before, and someone should press upon the joint on the table; and when the patient extends his legs, they should be even, then adjust the thighs and apply the plaster, and tighten it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and he should rest for three or four days, then release the bandage and apply the plaster again; and if you see that they are even, then tighten as before and let him rest for three days, then release the bandage and let him walk comfortably until his limbs are healed.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is, inside, outside, and behind; it is not dislocated in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not straighten at his thigh, then know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is that you make the patient sit up straight, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend both sides of the knee firmly; and another minister extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the signs are that it straightens his leg at his thigh lightly; and apply the plaster, and let the leg air-dry at the thigh, and keep them together tightly for three or four days, then release it; and the patient should not exert himself by walking until the limb is healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if there is no joint, then strong extension must be administered, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes crushed, and sometimes fully dislocated, inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it hurts when pressed on the affected part; the movements are slight, and one should gently extend it to their hands when it is only dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is healed all over, then you should make the patient stand upright, and press the leg firmly down on the ankle; then pull the foot towards your right hand, then your left, twice each way, and then stretch it upwards, and draw it up firmly; do this twice as we have said, by bending and stretching the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, repeat the procedure, because it will return; and if it still cannot be returned in this way, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and push the peg firmly into the ground between his buttocks, and wind cloth around it so that he does not move; then press one minister against the thigh, and another extends the foot towards their hands or the knee, which they hold onto the neck of the foot; then extend each minister equally, and the pegs are still between the patient's buttocks to hold him in place as they are stretched; then put the mirrors evenly at their hands, and one minister pushes the healthy leg down from below, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it has reached its peak, then place the plaster and padding on top, and tighten it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and be careful of the nerves that are behind the ankle, so that the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligature loosens, then tighten it again; then untie it after three or four days, and the patient should be able to walk within four days; and if he walks before this time, there is no guarantee that he will not relapse.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes, you must calm it down as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the arms
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the arms are dislocated, they should be stretched gently without force, and that is a minor issue.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in the lower back or foot, then you should make the patient lie flat on his back on a bed or table, and place your foot over the affected joint, then press firmly on your foot until it pops back into place; and when it is back in position and there is nothing protruding, place a board with two crossbeams under the sole of the foot, then tighten it firmly, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and have him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you want to restore it, many times the patient dies; so do not be presumptuous in the treatment if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it for long, nor pitiless and merciless, and do not be bold. Use hot abscess-calming remedies at first, and leave the patient in God's hand if you see no hope of recovery; but when you see hope, then immediately return the limb to its place so that the hot abscesses may heal; once the limb is in place, administer hot abscess-calming remedies and treat the wound as it requires with drying ointments. If there is fracturing and small bones are displaced, set the bones and do what we have said for simple fractures; and beware of taking a path of fear, as I have said, lest you suffer much according to your Creator, and for the sake of your soul and body.
Amen	So be it.
